The Shanghai Bank Qingyang Warehouse's establishment of branch warehouses in Sitoubei, Xizhang, etc. in this county should be notified to follow the procedures. (1) A cooperative operating an agricultural warehouse must limit its business to its members and submit a roster for reference.

Jiangyin

Major Fire at the Hengqin Factory in Nanwai 106

The Hengqin Dyeing and Weaving Factory in Fangjia Alley, Banqiao, Nanwai, was established by Xu Shoukang and Xing Mingqiu, natives of Xieyuan, with a capital of 40,000 yuan. It has been in operation for three years and is large in scale, with more than 60 power looms and its own engine generator. It has a wholesale office in Shanghai. Xing Mingqiu recently went to Shanghai to quit opium. The factory duties are being handled by Shou Kang's son, Sanbao. The factory's cloth sales are very good, and night shifts started last month. Yesterday (the 7th) around 5:00 PM, a fire suddenly broke out in the bobbin room of the factory. According to reports, the cause was a cigarette butt being dropped in a pile of yarn. Fearing losses, they did not announce it at the time, but ordered the factory workers to put out the fire themselves. By the time the flames broke through the roof, outsiders learned of it. Around 6:00 PM, the fire department was finally notified, and fire trucks rushed to the scene. The fire had already spread to the yarn accounting room and cloth room. Only the weaving room and outside accounting room were unaffected. At the same time, the houses of neighbors Xing Shuntai, Xing Sengui, Xing Shenzhi, Xing Shengzhen, Xing Shouqi, and tenants Zhu Jintang, Su Yangzhi, and Tan Abing, which were connected to the factory buildings, were also affected. A total of twenty-eight rooms were burned down. Together with the yarn, cloth, and equipment in the factory, the total loss was estimated at seventy to eighty thousand yuan. Fortunately, Hengqin had fire insurance. Xing Mingqiu in Shanghai has been telegraphed to return to Cheng to handle the matter. Work was temporarily suspended on the 8th. Work will resume after the fire scene has been cleared.

Changzhou

Fugitive Bandit Accomplice Fu Xiaogou Apprehended 107

Xu Baoguang, the director of the Wu County Public Security Bureau, recently received a tip-off that Fu Xiaogou and other accomplices of the fugitive bandit Ren Haoming were running a gambling den in Yangtianba in the Fifth District, and that the profits were being used to campaign for Ren Haoming's release. He requested that police be dispatched to arrest them. Director Xu dispatched Inspector Xu Shengting and Service Officer Cui Yulin, leading a team of more than thirty police officers. On the afternoon of the 6th, they took a car to Qishuyan, transferred to a boat, and landed at Hengshan Bridge. They walked to their destination, arriving around 3:00 AM on the 7th. They waited until dawn. When the teahouse clerk opened the door, they ordered him to lead the way. They then apprehended Fu Xiaogou. However, the gambling den had already closed down upon hearing the news. Inspector Xu and others took Fu Xiaogou back to the bureau for investigation.

Qingjiang

Course of Events of the Storm at Cheng Zhi Vocational School 108

At Huaiyin Private Cheng Zhi Vocational School, the third-year students, because they will be graduating next year, and the Department of Education has still not approved their registration, which will affect their chances of further education, suddenly launched a storm at 3:00 PM on the 5th. All the day students and some of the faculty and staff in the school climbed over the courtyard walls and fled. The troublemaking students then blockaded the school gates, preventing other students and faculty and staff from entering or leaving. Principal Zhang Shaonan, fearing that the storm would escalate, personally went to the county government and the Public Security Bureau to request assistance in maintaining order. Section Chief Fang and Inspector Chen went to the school to dissuade them. The students finally agreed to leave the school on the afternoon of the 6th. Principal Zhang and others then entered the school to inspect the damage, and found that many school properties had been damaged. Zhang, considering that it was difficult to resume classes at present, gave the students from distant places travel expenses and ordered them to return home. He would notify them to return to school for classes once everything had been tidied up. The storm came to an end.

Yangzhou

Large Batch of Opium Offenders Arrested and Escorted to the Province 109

Lu Dagou, the secretary of the Anti-Opium Committee of Jiangdu County, led armed police and assisted Ling Xixian, an official dispatched by the Provincial Committee, in searching for opium offenders. They first discovered eight small packages of opium and many opium paraphernalia in the underground cellar of Sun Yanwu's house in Dayuan. At the home of Liu Chen and Bao Sun in Xiaoyangrou Lane, they seized nine opium boards and many opium paraphernalia. At the home of Cao Guobao in Dongyuanmen Lantern Lane, they seized many hiding places, three pieces of opium, and many opium paraphernalia. Because Cao escaped, his grandmother Cao Zhang was detained and interrogated. On the morning of the 7th, a written report was prepared and police were dispatched to accompany Commissioners Ling to escort Sun Yanwu, Liu Chen, Bao Sun, Cao Zhang, opium, and opium paraphernalia to the province for interrogation.

Hangzhou

Elderly Woman Kills Herself by Worshiping Buddha 110

Gong Zhenglin, a resident of No. 63 Zhouwang Temple, Jianggan, is a driver on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway. His mother, Zhao, is 61 years old. She usually worships gods and Buddhas to excess and suffers from slight mental illness. At 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon, she felt slightly unwell after eating, so she went upstairs to sleep. When her daughter-in-law brought tea upstairs, she found her mother-in-law had hanged herself. She had been dead for some time and could not be saved. The police were notified and the Hangzhou District Court was notified to send officials to examine the body. Her son Zhenglin prepared a coffin for burial.

Provincial Government Clerk Investigated for Fraud 111

Li Xiaojin, a female student at the West Lake Art College in Hangzhou, was questioned by the Third Section of the Secretariat of the Provincial Government on suspicion of being a reactionary. She was ordered to be handed over for custody and supervision. Later, due to a case involving reactionary classmates, she was summoned by the Security Department and ordered to confess. Li then stated that on the day she was handed over for custody by the Third Section of the Secretariat of the Provincial Government, she had asked Long Jianxing, a clerk in the section, to ask a friend to explain the matter and had paid 130 yuan as a reward. Chairman Lu was furious upon hearing the news. He immediately ordered the guards to take Long into custody and personally issued an order for his dismissal. In addition to ordering Section Chief Cheng Ying to thoroughly investigate the matter, he ordered that the people, documents, and evidence be transferred to the High Court for interrogation yesterday.

Letter Received 112

Case of a letter from the Changyuan County Government: Received a telegram from Director Kong Jian of the Labor Relief Group of the National Government Yellow River Flood Relief Committee: "I have just read in Shen Bao, reporting that the Ji Provincial Government received a telegram from the Changyuan County Magistrate stating that the water flow at the breach in Longmenkou is turbulent, the water outside the city is one zhang higher than inside the city, and loopholes are being discovered in the city walls daily. The water is very large, and the entire city is in danger of being submerged. I checked the recent reports, the water level in Guantai has been declining daily. How could the water outside the county city still be one zhang higher than inside the city? Is what is reported true? Please investigate and reply by telegram." The above telegram was dispatched, and there is no such fact in this city either. I think it is an error in the reports of your newspaper. I am writing to request that you investigate and correct it, so as not to confuse listeners and cause misunderstandings. County Magistrate Zhang Qinglu.

Page 11

Local News

Yesterday's Memorial Service for Mr. Shi Liangcai Held by the Entire Staff of This Newspaper 113

A Total of 491 People Attended

Solemn, Orderly, and Well-Organized

Colleagues Vowed to Continue His Legacy

Telegrams Requested the Government to Intensify the Search for the Perpetrator

The entire staff of this newspaper held a memorial service for Mr. Shi Liangcai at the Lake Society Auditorium on Guizhou Road yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM. In addition to former colleague Mr. Guo Butao, a total of 491 staff members and workers attended, each wearing a memorial badge of Mr. Shi on their chest and black gauze on their arms to express their condolences. Two sets of sound equipment were installed in the hall by Asia America Company. Star Film Company also sent personnel to film the event for remembrance. On the spot, a unanimous resolution was passed to send telegrams to the Executive Yuan and the Military Affairs Commission, requesting a strict search for the perpetrator and a prompt resolution of the case to comfort his spirit. Finally, all the colleagues swore an oath in front of Mr. Shi's portrait, took photos, and distributed memorial books. The atmosphere was extremely solemn. The meeting ended at 3:30 PM. The details are recorded below:

Venue Arrangement 114

In front of the Inqishi Memorial Hall, a white cloth banner reading "Meeting of 'Shen Bao' Staff to Commemorate Mr. Shi Liangcai" was hung. A simple colored archway was erected at the entrance, and the character "Dian" [meaning offering/tribute] made of neon lights was installed at the entrance. This was a gift from the Daylai Neon Light Company of the Baiye Trading Company. The General Manager Huang Weichang and Chen Qiwei personally came to direct the installation, and their kindness was greatly appreciated. The meeting place was on the second floor. The altar in the main hall was made purely of pine and cypress branches, adorned with fresh flowers and blue electric lights in a semi-circular shape. The aisle was covered with blue and white silk, strewn with fresh flowers and leaves. In the center was a full-body three-dimensional portrait of Mr. Shi, surrounded by white silk, with the four characters "Ren Lun Shi Biao" [meaning a model of morality and virtue] inscribed on it. A white cloth banner reading "Spirit Immortal" hung in front of the altar. Each pillar in the hall was wrapped with pine, cypress, and bamboo branches. Over two hundred elegiac couplets and memorial banners written by colleagues were hung on the four walls upstairs and downstairs. The arrangement was simple and solemn, and the entire venue was quiet, naturally inspiring feelings of sorrow.

Assembly Order 115

(1) Ringing the bell to begin the meeting; (2) Chairman's report on the purpose of the meeting; (3) Playing mourning music; (4) All standing in silence for three minutes; (5) Offering flowers; (6) Reciting the biography; (7) Reading the memorial oration; (8) Playing mourning music; (9) Bowing three times; (10) Speeches; (11) Playing mourning music; (12) Family members' address; (13) Photography; (14) Adjournment.

Assembly Staff 116

Chairman: Zhang Yunhe; Master of Ceremonies: Jin Huating; Recorders: Zhu Mingxin, Huang Jiping; Accountants: Sun Jieren, Shan Qingtong, Li Songqing; Inspectors: Yao Zichu, Tang Ti Yun, Huang Xinde, Sun Guanying, Wang Meiting, Cheng Bojun; Documents: Xu Gancheng; Administrators: Huang Yanqing, Dai Yunqing, Song Yetang, Song Xuequan, Jiang Xianchun, Lu Taosheng, Xu Minchu, Qian Zhenwan, Qian Changzhong, Qian Meisheng; Photographer: Xu Tianzhang; Security: Xu Canting, Huang Pintang.

Chairman's Report 117

Chairman Mr. Zhang Yunhe reported on the purpose of the meeting, saying: Mr. Shi Liangcai, the General Manager of this newspaper, suddenly suffered a tragic incident on the Shanghai-Hangzhou road on the 13th of this month. Colleagues were shocked, grieved, and saddened upon hearing this. Mr. Shi's name is known in the world, and his contributions are to society. The career that Mr. Shi devoted his life's energy to is in public opinion. Naturally, there are many people who mourn upon hearing this news. However, we, the colleagues serving at the 'Shen Bao,' which Mr. Shi devoted his energy to, are with Mr. Shi day and night, and listened to his instructions daily, so we feel especially sorrowful and saddened. Therefore, we especially hold this public memorial service at the Hushe Guild Hall at 1 pm today to express our grief and remembrance.

Offering Wreaths 118

After the Chairman's report, mourning music was played loudly. After the music stopped, everyone stood up and observed three minutes of silence to mourn Mr. Shi. Then, Chairman Zhang Yunhe and Manager Ma Yinliang offered flowers. They held up a large character "Dian" [meaning offering/tribute] made of yellow and white chrysanthemums, bowed three times in front of Mr. Shi's spirit, and then withdrew.

Reading the Biography 119

Qian Hua read "The Life of Mr. Shi Liangcai," compiled by the funeral committee, saying: Mr. Shi Liangcai, named Jiuxiu, was known by his style name in middle age. His ancestral home was Jiangning. His father, Chunfan, suffered from the Taiping Rebellion and did business in Xisijing Town, Shanghai, and thus settled there. Mr. Shi was intelligent from a young age and studied under the respected scholar Dai Kuiren, reading books and remembering them after one glance. Xisijing belonged to Lou County, Songjiang Prefecture. In the spring of the 25th year of the Guangxu reign (Qing Dynasty), he was admitted to the Lou County school as a Supplementary Student. At that time, it was after the Wuxu Reform (Hundred Days' Reform). Mr. Shi was indignant at the corruption of the Qing Dynasty's politics and abandoned the path of imperial examination. Together with Lei Jixing and Gong Jingqing from Songcheng, he studied Japanese language and applied sciences such as physics and chemistry. In the autumn of the 27th year of the Guangxu reign, he and his fellow villager Wu Fengci were admitted to the Hangzhou Sericulture School. During a school break, he advocated for the establishment of schools and urged local elders to raise funds, which led to the establishment of the Yangzheng Primary School for the rice industry in Sijing, which is still thriving today. After Mr. Shi completed his studies at the Sericulture School, he was hired as a teacher of physics and chemistry at the Wang's Yucai School in Shanghai. He then held teaching positions at the Binggong School, Wuben Girls' School, and Nanyang Middle School. At that time, the imperial examination system had not yet been abolished. Mr. Shi was skilled in rhetoric and once gave a lecture at Yangzheng Primary School to enlighten the people, and the audience flocked to listen, all admiring his foresight. In the 30th year of the Guangxu reign, he founded the Women's Sericulture School in Guishu Lane, Gaochang Temple, Shanghai, which was the first women's sericulture education in our country. In the past thirty years, the prosperity of the sericulture industry in the counties around Taihu Lake has been greatly influenced by Mr. Shi. This school was later moved to Hushu Pass in Suzhou, which is now the Jiangsu Provincial Sericulture School. In the 31st year of the Guangxu reign, together with other comrades, he initiated the Jiangsu Educational Affairs General Association. Not long after, the proposal for Jiangsu and Zhejiang to borrow British funds to build roads arose. With the advocacy of Tang Dianxian, Zhang Jian, Wang Dankui and other elders, the public gathered funds to build the roads themselves. Mr. Shi was one of the most active in this endeavor. After the company was established, he was elected as a director. At that time, Mr. Shi also served as the chief writer for the Shibao newspaper and had already developed a deep interest in the news industry. In his spare time, he initiated the National Agricultural Affairs Federation in Nanjing and was elected as the general manager. When Nanjing held the Nanyang Industrial Exposition, Mr. Shi gathered agricultural experts to participate in the examination and research. Soon after, the revolutionary army in Wuhan launched an uprising, and the provinces responded. The leaders in Jiangsu were Cheng Xuelou, Zhang Jian, Ying Jizhong and other gentlemen. Mr. Shi participated in all consultations. However, at that time, talents gathered, and Mr. Shi was particularly praised for his keen thinking and precise governance. Therefore, the Jianghai Customs property was as tangled as a ball of thread, and the Shanghai Customs Clearance Office was established, with Mr. Shi in charge. The salt administration in Songjiang needed to be reorganized, and the Songjiang Salt Bureau was established, with Mr. Shi as its head. Mr. Shi focused on social undertakings, believing that the rise of a country was based on culture, and that promoting culture required the media as the vanguard. Therefore, in the first year of the Republic of China (1912), he took over the Shen Bao newspaper, which was struggling. For more than twenty years, he never slackened, truly pouring his life's blood into it. When Yuan Shikai stole the country and offered a large sum of money to order him not to oppose the imperial system, Mr. Shi refused directly. Subsequently, the warlords ruled the country for ten years. He remained upright and clean, and careful and self-preserving, which took a lot of effort. Mr. Shi also believed that enterprise creation was the foundation of a wealthy and prosperous country. In the tenth year of the Republic of China (1921), he co-founded the Zhongnan Bank with the overseas Chinese businessman Huang Yizhu. In the same year, he initiated the Minsheng Cotton Mill. He also assisted Xiang Songmao in expanding the business of the Wuzhou Pharmacy, and assisted Lufei Bohong in reviving the Zhonghua Book Company. Everything he planned prospered. People therefore admired Mr. Shi's talents and courage. Mr. Shi focused on stability and further expanded the newspaper business. In his spare time, he visited both Daoist and Buddhist temples, consulted classics, and practiced meditation. After more than ten years of dedicated cultivation, he gained considerable peace and tranquility. He also learned boxing and fighting skills, and his agility was unmatched, even surpassing that of young people. After the September 18th Incident (Mukden Incident), Mr. Shi was greatly indignant and gathered comrades day and night to discuss how to assist the government in saving the country. After the January 28th Incident (Shanghai Incident) broke out, the Shanghai Citizens' Local Maintenance Association was organized, and he was elected as its chairman. After the association was reorganized and renamed the Shanghai Municipal Local Association, he was still elected as its chairman. The government especially valued Mr. Shi. The Rural Reconstruction Committee hired him as a member, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was reorganized into a state-owned enterprise and he was hired as a director, and the Ministry of Industry planned to establish the Wenxi Paper Mill and hired him as the deputy director of the preparatory committee. The Shanghai Municipal Government established a temporary Municipal Council and hired him as a councilor, and he was elected as the speaker. Mr. Shi deeply felt the mutual respect from both the government and the public, which motivated him to work harder. He never declined any position in economic, cultural, and charitable organizations. For example, he was elected as a director of the New China Cultural Association and as a standing director of the Zhongshan Cultural Education Center. His constant concern was for the Northeast, and he founded the Northeast Refugee Relief Association with his comrades, hoping to alleviate the suffering of the refugees. His participation in other public welfare undertakings cannot be fully described. Since he studied physics and chemistry at an early age, he would support any scientific inventions, even with heavy financial assistance. As for the Shen Bao, which he independently managed, after holding the 60th anniversary celebration, he was determined to expand the affiliated businesses, such as the continuing education school, circulating library, yearbook, and monthly magazine. He also hired experts to produce detailed national maps, all of which made great contributions to enlightening people and culture. He worked tirelessly day and night, exhausting his mental and physical strength, and often suffered from stomach ailments. He took the time to go to West Lake in Hangzhou to rest and recuperate. Unexpectedly, on his way back to Shanghai from Hangzhou, near Wengjiabu Dazhakou in Haining, he encountered many bandits and was assassinated. This happened at 3:00 pm on November 13th of the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1934). He was only fifty-six years old.

Reading the Memorial Oration 120

The entire staff of the Shen Bao newspaper offered a memorial oration to Mr. Shi, saying: On December 8th of the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1934), we respectfully offer pure wine and delicacies to the spirit of Mr. Shi Liangcai, saying: Ah, our Mr. Shi, the hope of the nation, with broad capabilities and extensive knowledge, truly a gift from heaven. Intelligent and exceptional from a young age, praised and admired by all in the neighborhood. Outstanding among peers, talents and heroes vied to recommend him, seeing him as a man of great potential, capable of shouldering great responsibilities. Dedicated to public welfare, he firmly established his will, and amidst the clamor of worldly pursuits, he did not let it cloud his nature. Gifted in writing from a young age, he was able to adapt to change. With great foresight, his eyes were like torches. Lamenting the ignorance of the times, and the downward flow of society, he corrected wrongs and guided goodness, on which the people relied. With the publication of each paper, the masses were inspired. The continuation and expansion of glory was mainly due to Mr. Shi. Establishing the norms and principles, he illuminated the path. His heart and soul nurtured and cultivated, resulting in the flourishing of the newspaper. With a voice to speak out, he strived to enlighten the people, cultivate talent, and promote education, benefiting all. His good reputation was widely spread, and both the public and private sectors sought his advice. He listened to the opinions of the people, and made suggestions to the government. Mr. Shi was never complacent. With remaining energy, he thought of doing more, relieving disasters and helping the needy, opening up granaries. All his great achievements are clearly visible. His love and kindness were bestowed on the people, and no one should dare to insult him. How could such a virtuous man be envied by the wicked? Poisonous hands and old grudges plotted secretly, attacking from all sides. A sudden storm arose, and he met with such a tragic end. The dying words of Lord Mengchang [a famous historical figure] echo through the ages. With Mr. Shi's age and strength, there was still much to be done. To be cut down so early, what can we say? We are unworthy, but honored to know him and cherish our old friendship. Hearing the news of his death, we were caught unprepared, unable to save him. We express our sorrow with our words, feeble as they may be. We offer this memorial, hoping his spirit will acknowledge it. Alas! May you enjoy this offering. After reading, the entire assembly stood and bowed three times. Then, speeches were given by colleagues.

Summary of Speeches 121

First, Mr. Guo Butao of the Xinwen Bao newspaper, a former colleague of this newspaper, gave a speech, saying in brief, Mr. Liangcai died an unnatural death, and everyone, whether acquainted or not, mourns with one voice. Mr. Shi dedicated his life's work to the benefit of society. His sudden misfortune is a great loss to Chinese society. But since things have come to this, instead of passive sorrow, we should actively strive to continue Mr. Shi's unfinished will. In my opinion, "sacrifice" has two interpretations: one is a meaningful sacrifice, and the other is a meaningless sacrifice. Mr. Shi's death is a meaningful sacrifice. Nothing in this world can succeed without sacrifice. Without sacrifice, there is no hope of success. For example, to make a table, we must first sacrifice trees, sacrifice labor, and sacrifice paint before it can be made. Everything we need in our daily lives, such as food, clothing, shelter, and transportation, inevitably sacrifices various substances. Extending this to all the contributions of mankind worldwide, has there ever been a moment without sacrificing the infinite energy of the sages and philosophers to develop today's civilization? The annals of history, both Chinese and foreign, can serve as evidence. For example, Jesus sacrificed himself on the cross, and his great spirit of universal love can move all mankind. The compassionate essence of Buddhism has been passed down for thousands of years and has not waned to this day. Confucius is a model for all generations and was also the person with the greatest spirit of sacrifice in his time. He did not avoid any hardship, and his doctrines are admired both in China and abroad. It can be seen that the two words "sacrifice" have always been the same throughout history. Mr. Liangcai was a famous figure of his time and a pioneer in the newspaper industry. Unfortunately, he sacrificed his life. Although his body is dead, his spirit shines brightly both in China and abroad and will never die. How should we continue his legacy and carry forward his work? Those of you here cannot shirk this responsibility. Therefore, I say that the meaning of commemoration is not in form but in the efforts of the spirit. May you continue Mr. Shi's legacy and strive forward so as not to betray the original intention of commemoration.

(2) Mr. Ma Yinliang, manager of this newspaper, said in a brief speech: Mr. Shi loved the colleagues of this newspaper the most. Now that Mr. Shi has unfortunately passed away, I hope that all colleagues will love the Shen Bao with the same heart that Mr. Shi loved us. Then, even though Mr. Shi is dead, his spirit will not die. What I hope for even more from my colleagues is that we not only maintain the Shen Bao but also do our best to make it progress and develop. Then, Mr. Shi's spirit will not only not die, but it will also have a day to flourish and be carried forward.

(3) Mr. Qu Shaoyi of the editorial department of this newspaper said in a brief speech: Mr. Shi's death is recognized as a great loss to society. There are indeed not many people today who are engaged in social undertakings with the same enthusiasm and perseverance as Mr. Shi. Mr. Shi did not reach the age of longevity and could have continued to serve society. Now, due to an extraordinary change, society has lost a mentor, which is truly regrettable. Therefore, those who mourn Mr. Shi are not only the colleagues of the entire newspaper but also the people of society, who deeply express their grief and regret. Mr. Shi has left us. Those who survive should rise up and strive to maintain his career forever without decay. The success of a social undertaking is difficult for the creator, and it is also difficult for the maintainer. Mr. Shi was the creator, and we are the maintainers. In the future, if there are people who will take over the responsibility for the social undertaking, then the achievements of the creator will never be extinguished through the ages. The colleagues of this newspaper have always held the purpose of assisting Mr. Shi's career. Although Mr. Shi has passed away, his spirit will remain forever in the world, and his career will last forever in society. If we can all work together, it will be enough to repay Mr. Shi.

(4) Mr. Zhang Zisheng, Director of the Shen Bao Yearbook Society, spoke of his personal admiration for Mr. Shi's daily cultivation and practice, saying: Mr. Shi often studied Buddhist scriptures in his spare time, and his cultivation was deeply influenced by Buddhism. Therefore, he could understand the true meaning of the word "diligence" in Buddhism, so he could strive to be proactive, abandon the interests of the "small self," and consider the welfare of society, and strive to run various undertakings. Because he was deeply helped by the four words "see one's mind and realize one's nature" in Buddhism, he could see things clearly, and could make decisions on all matters with one word. Now that Mr. Shi has passed away, his cultivation and practice can serve as a model for his colleagues to emulate. I hope that colleagues will carry forward the Shen Bao's business with the spirit of "diligence" and observe all related issues with the effort of "seeing one's mind and realizing one's nature."

(5) Mr. Yu Zhonghua, Director of the Shen Bao Monthly Magazine Society, said briefly: On this day when the colleagues of this newspaper are commemorating Mr. Shi, each and every one of us feels heartbroken and grieved. Although I and the colleagues of the Monthly Magazine Society have only been in the newspaper for more than two years, our qualifications in the newspaper are very shallow, but we are very heartbroken for Mr. Shi's tragic assassination. So I know that the colleagues who are old-timers in the newspaper must be even more grieved. I have thousands of words to say about Mr. Shi's unfortunate death, but in sorrow, I feel that there is nothing to say, so I will now only report to you a conversation that Mr. Shi had this summer. "A friend, Mr. Ma Xingye, majored in journalism in the United States. He graduated and returned to China this summer. When he arrived in Shanghai, he wanted Mr. Ma Yinliang and me to introduce him to Mr. Shi and Mr. Zhang to talk. We first introduced him to Mr. Zhang, and then Mr. Ma Yinliang and I introduced him to the Shi's residence to talk. When Mr. Shi saw him, he told him about his experience in running a newspaper. Mr. Shi said that the newspaper is like a large glass jar that is easy to break. I have been holding the historical Shen Bao for more than 20 years, and I have finally managed not to break it. Now I have held it until I am covered in sweat. I am old, and in the future, this Shen Bao will be held by many old colleagues in the newspaper. He also said that Mr. Zhang has been the same for decades, and Mr. Ma Yinliang has also been actively fighting for the newspaper. Running a newspaper requires perseverance, and Mr. Zhang's decades of consistency are truly admirable." Who would have thought that only a few months later, the words were still in our ears, and unfortunately Mr. Shi has passed away and can no longer hold the Shen Bao, and this Shen Bao really has to rely on the old colleagues in the newspaper to hold it up. When you hear my brief report, you will definitely be even more saddened, but I believe that after you are saddened, all of you, all the old-timers, will also feel the great responsibility, because in the past, the Shen Bao was held by Mr. Shi like holding a glass jar. Now, the Shen Bao has to be held jointly by all of you colleagues, especially the old-timers. Mr. Shi had many businesses during his lifetime, but the business that he put his heart and soul into was the Shen Bao. I believe that the human body sometimes comes to an end, but the spirit is immortal forever. The body can be destroyed by assassination, but the spirit cannot be eliminated by bullets, because the body can be destroyed, but the spirit cannot be eliminated, so the spirit is immortal forever. Therefore, I believe that if you want to commemorate Mr. Shi, you must maintain the Shen Bao well, and to carry forward Mr. Shi's immortal spirit, you must also maintain the Shen Bao well. If you old-timers can take on the responsibility of maintaining the Shen Bao, it is the best way to commemorate Mr. Shi and the most powerful proof that Mr. Shi's spirit is immortal.

(6) Mr. Zhou Shoujuan, editor of the Shen Bao Chunqiu supplement, said briefly: Mr. Shi suddenly died in an accident on the Shanghai-Hangzhou National Road on the afternoon of November 13th. I learned of the bad news that evening at a friend's house. At first, I thought it was inaccurate, and when I arrived at the newspaper, the news had been confirmed. I was inexplicably grieved. The West has always considered "thirteen" an ominous word, but the Chinese do not always believe it. Now that Mr. Shi has unfortunately died on the 13th, he is considered a pessimist. Those who view life and death as not being important, but at this time when the national crisis is serious, we should be inspired to find a way to break the national crisis. I personally feel that the gunshots on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road are just like the gunshots in Zhabei during the "January 28th" incident. The gunshots in Zhabei damaged China's vitality and destroyed our cultural undertakings, and the gunshots on the Hangzhou-Shanghai Road killed the authority of our newspaper industry. The meaning and tragedy are equally significant, making me remember it forever and never forget it. Mr. Shi was harmed, but he can be said to have sacrificed himself for the Shen Bao. Now that Mr. Shi is gone, we should follow the bloodstains of the martyrs and work hard to comfort the spirit of the hero, etc.

Colleagues' Oath 122

At the end, Mr. Xu Deliang, a colleague of this newspaper, made a temporary proposal: (1) Send a telegram to the Executive Yuan of the National Government and the Military Affairs Commission, requesting them to quickly arrest the murderers and solve the case; (2) The colleagues took an oath in front of the spirit to express their unified attitude. The oath reads: "We swear with sincerity to continue the legacy of General Manager Shi, to fight actively, this oath."

Telegram Requesting Arrest of Murderers 123

To President Wang and Chairman Jiang of Nanjing: Mr. Shi Liangcai, the General Manager of this newspaper, was murdered. We are grateful for your clear orders to arrest the murderers, but nearly a month has passed and they have not yet been caught. Today, all employees held a meeting to commemorate and unanimously decided to send a telegram requesting you to strictly order your subordinates to intensify the investigation to clear the injustice and uphold the law. We are overwhelmed with anticipation. Zhang Yunhe, Ma Yinliang, and 491 others from the Shen Bao Newspaper respectfully kowtow.

Family Members' Response 124

Finally, Mr. Shi Jiangguang gave a response on behalf of Mr. Shi's family, saying: "My uncle unfortunately passed away. Thank you to all the colleagues for holding this memorial meeting. We are grateful in life and death. My uncle dedicated his life to the newspaper industry, and half his life to the serious business of the Shen Bao. I hope that in the future, you colleagues will continue to love my uncle and love and carry forward the Shen Bao. Then, my uncle's spirit in the afterlife will surely smile in the nine springs. Thank you all for your kindness." He bowed three times and withdrew. The entire assembly was photographed, and the meeting adjourned.

Condolence Letters from Various Regions 125

Xu Hanting of the Zhangshu branch of the Shen Bao in Jiangxi wrote: Respectful greetings to Mr. Yonggeng of the Shen Bao Newspaper: I was shocked and deeply saddened to hear of the misfortune of your father. I send this telegram to express my condolences. Xu Hanting of the Zhangshu Town Shen Bao branch kowtows, November 29th.

Zhao and Huang, reporters of the Huanghai Tide News in Weihaiwei, wrote: Respectful greetings to Mr. Yonggeng: We recently read the newspaper and were shocked to learn that your father, Mr. Liangcai, had suffered an unexpected misfortune. We are deeply saddened. We imagine that we colleagues in the newspaper industry have suddenly lost our teacher. How unfortunate is that! We hope that you will restrain your grief and accept the changes so that you can avenge this great hatred. We send this condolence letter specifically, and we hope that you will acknowledge it. Zhao Lengxian and Huang Moqiao, reporters of the Huanghai Tide News in Weihaiwei, pay their respects together, December 1st.

Xu Xishan of the Xinghua Shen Bao distribution point wrote: To Mr. Yonggeng of the Shi's residence, c/o the Shanghai Shen Bao Newspaper: Respectful greetings, I am writing to inform you that since hearing the news, we have been deeply concerned and grieved. Your late father participated in almost every undertaking that was beneficial to society. His enthusiasm was known to all, both in China and abroad. Unexpectedly, he was assassinated on the way back home on the Shanghai-Hangzhou road, which is extremely painful. We are separated by mountains and rivers and cannot attend the funeral service in person. We are very sorry. We respectfully send a elegiac couplet, hoping it will be hung on the right side of the spirit to express our respect and grief. We send this letter respectfully and wish you well. Xu Xishan of the Xinghua Shen Bao distribution point bows, December 5th.

Affiliated Cultural Organizations of Shen Bao Will Commemorate Mr. Shi Tomorrow 126

Location: Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association

Time: 9:00 AM

The Shen Bao Circulating Library, Amateur Continuing Education School, and Women's Continuing Education School, the three cultural organizations, are deeply saddened by the tragic assassination of Mr. Shi Liangcai, the founder of these organizations, on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway. The circulating library has had over 10,000 readers, and the amateur continuing education school with its six branches and the women's continuing education school have over 2,000 students. Under the atmosphere of grief, they jointly initiated the organization of a memorial meeting. They convened the first preparatory meeting on November 24th and appointed responsible personnel for each section to carry out the work separately. They have been actively preparing in recent days and are almost ready. The date of the meeting is set for December 10th at 9:00 AM, and the location is the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association on Xizang Road. Recently, the Shen Bao Circulating Library at the Nanjing Road Continental Emporium and the Shen Bao Women's Continuing Education School at Xieqiao Alley on Jing'an Temple Road have received a large number of elegiac couplets and memorial banners from students and readers of various schools. Xiao Zhenying Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday to Discuss the Process of Representing Chiang Kai-shek in Mongolia for Comforting and Appeasement 137

Transmitting the Central Government's Intentions to Jointly Consolidate the Border Areas

The Current Situation in Chahar Province is Peaceful and Finances Can Still Be Maintained

Song Zheyuan, Chairman of Chahar Province and Representative of the Peiping Readjustment Committee, Xiao Zhenying, recently represented Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and accompanied De Wang from Sui to Mongolia to inspect the recent situation in Inner Mongolia and convey the Central Government's intentions in order to jointly consolidate and unite the border areas. He has already completed his work, went south from Ping, and went to Beijing to report to Chiang Kai-shek on the inspection process. After completing his official duties in Beijing, he specially came to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday. He received the reporters of the Shen Shi News Agency at the hotel and talked about the mission to Inner Mongolia and the current situation of the military and political affairs of Mongolia and Chahar. The details are as follows:

Comforting and Appeasing Mongolia to Consolidate the Border Areas 138

According to Xiao, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek wanted to understand the real situation of political affairs in various parts of the country and inspect the northwest border areas in order to establish a practical link between the central government and the border areas. Therefore, when Chairman Chiang Kai-shek arrived in Suiyuan, he intended to go to Mongolia to thoroughly understand the current situation in Inner Mongolia. Mongolia is an important barrier for our country and is of great importance. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek paid great attention to this. However, due to time constraints, he could not go in person. At that time, De Wang and others had heard the news and went to Sui to pay their respects and had detailed discussions on Mongolian political affairs. In the past, no important government officials had personally inspected the Inner Mongolia border area. The result of this meeting between Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and De Wang completely eliminated the isolation between the central government and Inner Mongolia. Chiang Kai-shek also gave sincere instructions on the future policy of Mongolian affairs. Afterwards, in order to express the central government's concern for Mongolian political affairs, Chiang Kai-shek specially ordered me to accompany De Wang to Mongolia to convey the central government's intentions and discuss unity methods with the leaders of various banners to consolidate the border areas.

The Impression of Inspecting Inner Mongolia is Very Good 139

This time I went to Mongolia and have discussed the future of Mongolian political affairs and the implementation of policies with the leaders of various banners. I have also conveyed the central government's intentions for Mongolian affairs and how to seek organizational unity methods. De Wang and others have expressed their willingness to cooperate sincerely with the central government. After the establishment of the Inner Mongolia Autonomous Committee, it has achieved considerable results. As for the entire method of Mongolian political affairs, it still needs to be continued. According to my inspection this time, the current situation in Inner Mongolia is that the area is as vast as an boundless ocean. It is not easy for foreigners to occupy it. The people of Mongolia are mostly nomadic, scattered and not concentrated. All urban construction, etc., also lack a central point of assembly. Therefore, it is difficult to easily control it in military and political affairs. In the past, our country did not pay close attention to it, which led to the coveting of others and the use of various enticing methods to try to win over the Mongolian people and manipulate everything, such as the Japanese setting up "Neighborly Cooperation Cooperatives" everywhere in Inner Mongolia to sell cheap goods to the Mongolian people on credit, and setting up hospitals and distributing medicines in order to change the mentality of the Mongolian people. This is indeed a serious danger, but most of the Mongolian people have no good feelings towards the Japanese. As for our country in the past, although there was a lack of close contact, they still have a good concept of us. Therefore, it is now urgent for our government and people to pay attention to it and promote their unity, and then seek closer cooperation with our country.

Recent Situation in Chahar Province 140

Xiao continued, the current situation in Chahar Province is still without special changes. In the Chahar-Rehe border area, the Japanese and puppet troops often appear and provoke our army. It is difficult to determine whether they have copied the old habits and attempts of the four eastern provinces, but after our calm response, there is no other danger. As for Chairman Song, he has always adhered to a consistent proposition, protecting the territory and securing the people, and being cautious in handling affairs, so he can maintain the current peaceful situation within Chahar Province. Currently, Chahar Province has four divisions and two mixed brigades. The military expenses are all allocated by the Peiping Military Branch. The financial situation in Chahar Province is that the income is not abundant due to the barren area, but it can still be maintained with savings and response.

This Trip is to Report to Chiang Kai-shek on the Mission 141

Finally, according to Xiao's statement to the Shen Shi News Agency reporters, the mission of this trip south is purely to go to Beijing to report to Chiang Kai-shek on the process of the trip to Mongolia. He has already reported the details in Beijing and the work has been completed. Therefore, he took the opportunity to come to Shanghai to visit old friends. There are no other tasks. He plans to take the night express train back to Beijing tonight and leave Beijing for the north after the Fifth Plenary Session.

Pirate Riding Incident on the Zhejiang Sea, Shibu Ocean, on the Xinhai Gate Wheel 150

Passengers and Goods Were Looted

One Navigation Police Officer Was Killed

Six Crew Members and Passengers Were Kidnapped

New Voice News Agency reports that the headquarters of the Haimen Shipping Company is located in Ningbo. The Xinhai Gate Wheel has a deadweight of more than 400 tons and specializes in sailing between Ningbo and Wenzhou. On the 6th of this month, it was fully loaded with passengers and goods and departed from Ningbo. By 2:00 AM on the 7th, when passing through Shibu, more than 20 pirates disguised themselves as passengers and sneaked in. At that time, it was not discovered. After leaving Shibu, at about 2:00 PM, the pirates who had sneaked in fired a shot as a signal and began to ride and loot.

Navigation Police Killed. The Xinhai Gate Wheel was not equipped with anti-theft equipment and only sent four escort police officers to protect the ship. When the pirates were riding and looting, they first monitored the shipowner and the escort police officers. The navigation police resisted and one was killed by the pirates. The rest surrendered their weapons. Three or four passengers and teahouse staff were injured by stray bullets. More than 100 passengers were looted. About 300 pieces of goods in the ship, such as cotton yarn, cloth, and groceries, were also looted.

Before leaving, the ship sailed to Niushenmen Yangmian Gate and forced it to stop. They loaded the looted property into the pirate ship prepared in advance. Before leaving, they also kidnapped the comprador Zhang Akun and six passengers. The ship sailed as usual and arrived at Haimen on the evening of the 7th, and immediately telegraphed the Ningbo headquarters to report the looting. It is reported that the company has telegraphed the military police on various shores to strictly arrest the pirates and rescue the kidnapped people.

Zhou Bingchen of the Samsung Stage Is Accused of Fraudulently Obtaining Property 151

Absconded After Receiving the Deposit

Plaintiff Demands Compensation of 20,000 Yuan

The Beijing Opera House of the Samsung Stage on Niuzhuang Road in the British Concession was originally established by Zhou Bingchen, Zhao Ruquan, and the late Huang Chu Jiu. At the beginning of the cooperation, a Samsung Real Estate Company was also organized. All the houses adjacent to the theater were the property of the company. Later, after Huang Chu Jiu passed away, Zhao Ruquan and Zhou did not agree and went to court last winter. As a result of the lawsuit, Zhao's shares were also merged into Zhou's, so from this year on, all the Samsung Company and the Samsung Stage belonged to Zhou alone. However, Zhou's financial resources have never been very strong, and the theater's business has become increasingly declining. The shape of the exhausted state has become increasingly exposed recently. Zhou has no power to support it, and began in September to sell the theater and all the adjacent houses to Pang Laichen, a wealthy merchant from Nanxun in Shanghai. The price was agreed at 270,000 yuan, and Pang first gave a

Deposit of 100,000 yuan, and the remaining 170,000 yuan was collected by Mann, a British staff member of the Water Company, entrusted by Zhou. Before the sale, Zhou had mortgaged the real estate to Mann. However, Zhou also worked at the Water Company in the past, and had a close friendship with Mann, and they often communicated and helped each other in times of need. In the mortgage of Samsung's real estate to Mann, a part of the money was Zhou's private property. Zhou entrusted Mann to collect the 170,000 yuan of land price, and wanted to exchange the real estate certificate with him, hand it over to the buyer, and settle the accounts between them. Unexpectedly, after the settlement, the amount of money that Zhou wanted to find was more than 50,000 yuan more than what Mann found. Zhou was unwilling to sacrifice a huge amount of money, so he wrote to the buyer Pang Laichen, stating that he would revoke the power to entrust Mann to collect the money, and requested that the 170,000 yuan still be paid to him for collection. However, Pang believed that this entrustment and collection procedure was a condition agreed upon by the three parties, and

There was a contract that was still wet with ink, and he suddenly went back on his word, lost faith in foreigners, which was definitely not what he wanted. He strictly rejected Zhou's request, saying that he must follow the agreed terms. Zhou then filed a lawsuit against Pang for not paying the property price. The First Special District Local Court summoned the plaintiff, the defendant, and the important witness Mann to investigate. It was ruled that the agreed entrustment and collection contract should not be overturned, and the plaintiff lost the lawsuit. Zhou failed, and there was no hope for the property price at present, the economy was still in panic, and the debt was piled up, and he had to find another way out to raise funds. When he sold the real estate, he believed that the Samsung Stage was created by him, and did not want the stage to disappear with the property rights. After discussing and agreeing with Pang, he signed another lease contract and leased the stage to him for continued business. Now that he has lost the lawsuit,

There is no way to raise funds, so he had to ask Weng Xieyao and Zhu Shuzhu to mediate, and sell all the stage properties, scenery, and costumes of the theater to Gu Zhuxuan, the owner of the Tianchan Stage, for Gu to continue performing at the original site. The price was set at 36,000 yuan, and Gu paid a deposit of 10,000 yuan on the 20th of last month, all of which were Jifeng Qianzhuang's bank notes, divided into one sheet of 5,000 yuan, one sheet of 3,000 yuan, and two sheets of 1,000 yuan, with the payment date set on the 30th of last month. Zhou noted in the receipt issued for receiving the deposit that he would sign a formal sales contract within three days. After three days, Zhou suddenly absconded, neither signing the contract nor returning the bank notes. Although Gu repeatedly urged the two intermediaries to negotiate with Zhou, he could not find him and could not find any clues. Gu hired a lawyer to write to Jifeng, asking not to pay the money for the bank notes. Later, the bank replied that the nature of the bank notes was not like checks, and if he insisted on stopping the payment, he needed a court order to stop the payment. Therefore, Gu filed a

Criminal lawsuit against Zhou for fraudulently obtaining property in the First Special District Local Court, and said that when negotiating the sale, they had agreed with each other that no matter which party regretted it, they should be punished twice as much as the deposit. Therefore, in addition to asking the defendant to be punished in accordance with Article 363 of the Criminal Law, the defendant should be ordered to compensate the loss of 20,000 yuan, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng opened a court hearing. The defendant Zhou Bingchen did not attend, and only the plaintiff's lawyer and the two witnesses, Weng and Zhu, attended the court. They briefly described the situation of Zhou entrusting them to discuss the sale of the theater property with Gu, and said that the Samsung Stage has stopped business yesterday, and Zhou Bingchen has disappeared, requesting that a warrant be issued for his arrest, etc. Judge Huang then ordered that the hearing be postponed to the afternoon of December 15. The plaintiff should surrender himself to the court for questioning on the due date.

The Court Approves the Divorce Case of Liu Mingzhu and Her Husband 152

The Woman Subsidizes Medical Expenses of 1,500 Yuan

The Eight-Year-Old Daughter Is Raised by the Plaintiff Until Adulthood

Calculation Method for Names in Foreign Telegrams 154

Full Spelling Counts as One Word

Abbreviations Calculated Separately

Effective from the 10th

Regarding the calculation of fees for commonly used abbreviations and combined words in foreign telegrams, the Ministry of Transportation previously did not provide illustrative examples, leading to numerous confusions and disputes when various sectors sent such telegrams at telegraph offices. A special order is now issued to all telegraph offices, stipulating that connected words within such telegrams should be charged per word unless proven to be a registered telegraphic address. This applies whether the words are used in the address, message, or signature. For example, "Georgesmitb" should be counted as two words, "Hgwells" as three words, etc. Furthermore, for Chinese names translated into English, full spellings such as "Wangpaosung" are specially permitted to be counted as one word. However, abbreviated names such as "Pswang," whether in the telegraph address, message, or signature, should be counted as three words to comply with the provisions of the International Telegraph Convention's auxiliary telegraph regulations. It is also reported that the local telegraph office has received orders and distributed them to all receiving and sending clerks, to be uniformly implemented starting from the 10th of this month.

The number of poor in this session is greater than before, otherwise, financial difficulties are feared.

Both Railway Bureaus Revise Baggage Handling Fees 156

Regardless of Object Size

Twelve Copper Coins for All

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations recently announced regulations for baggage and package handling fees, to be implemented starting from the 10th of this month. The announcement states that the coolies at each station of the two railways will charge the following fees for handling baggage and packages, effective from the 10th of this month: (1) Regardless of the size of the baggage, each piece will be charged twelve copper coins. For packages weighing 60 kilograms or less, each piece will be charged eight copper coins. For packages weighing over 60 kilograms up to 120 kilograms, twelve copper coins will be charged. If coolies at this station engage in extortion, please report it to the responsible personnel at the respective station for strict reprimand. This announcement.

Discussion Meeting of the Industrial and Commercial Management Association 157

The Chinese Industrial and Commercial Management Association held its 53rd luncheon discussion meeting at noon yesterday in the east hall on the ninth floor of the YMCA in Eight Immortals Bridge. More than thirty people attended, including Li Zhaohuan, Lu Meiseng, Cao Yunxiang, Wu Yun Chu, Fang Zhicheng, Li Shouzhong, and Tang Zeyan. During the meeting, Tang Zeyan, secretary of the Industrial and Commercial Management Association, presided over the event, and Lu Meiseng, professor at Great China University, gave a speech on "Advertising and Sales Problems." The speech briefly stated that advertising already existed in the Greek era five thousand years ago, but it was not until 1911 that scientific methods were used to publish advertisements. The United States spends ten billion US dollars annually on advertising, which China cannot compare to. However, the purpose of advertising is to achieve broad effects. Therefore, advertising studies encompass psychology, literature, fine arts, economics, and commerce, and it is by no means something everyone can do. The current shortcomings of advertising in China are: (1) lack of system, (2) lack of order, (3) lack of planning, (4) lack of purpose, so advertising is mostly wasteful. Although schools have gradually introduced this course, it has not yet received sufficient attention.

New Life Collective Marriage Measures 161

Advocated by the Social Affairs Bureau

Mayor Wu Appreciates

Since the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs advocated the New Life collective marriage, all sectors have paid close attention, recognizing it as a necessary measure to shift extravagant customs and maintain the people's economy. It is learned that the Bureau of Social Affairs has submitted a draft plan to the Municipal Government for review. Mayor Wu also expressed his appreciation. The situation obtained from the Bureau of Social Affairs is as follows:

Reasons for Initiation According to a spokesperson for the Bureau of Social Affairs, the bureau has always paid great attention to the improvement of marriage ceremonies in the city. Recently, it has been noted that customs are becoming increasingly extravagant, and the cost of marriage often amounts to thousands. Although citizens have a strong desire for frugal marriages, they ultimately dare not set an example for fear of being despised by relatives and friends. Now is the time to actively promote the New Life Movement, and it is necessary for the government to promote frugal marriages to make them easier to popularize among the people. The use of collective marriage is to make the married person understand that he/she is a member of society, and to extend the concept of family to the concept of society. The previous report stated that the New Life collective marriage would follow the Italian method, which is not true, because Italy is limited to party members, while the city has no such restrictions, and the nature is completely different. Once this method is approved by the Municipal Government, registration will begin. After the city's trial implementation, it is hoped that provinces and cities will follow up to shift extravagance.

Draft Measures The draft measures are divided into three parts. The first part is the application for registration, which is divided into eight articles: (1) Citizens of the city who hold a wedding ceremony may apply to participate in the collective wedding ceremony. (2) The collective wedding ceremony is scheduled to be held in the City Hall Auditorium on New Year's Day, the anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's birth, Confucius' birthday, and National Day, and will be officiated by the mayor and the director of the Bureau of Social Affairs. (3) Participants should pay a fee of 20 yuan per person. (4) Participants should first apply to the Bureau of Social Affairs for approval. The application form can be obtained from the Bureau of Social Affairs in person and is free of charge. If the quota is full or there are doubts about the applicant, the application may be rejected. (5) Applicants who are approved for registration will be issued a registration certificate by the Bureau of Social Affairs and will participate with the registration certificate on the due date. (7) Applicants should strictly abide by the "Instructions for Participating in the New Life Collective Marriage" and comply with all times and procedures. (8) Marriage certificates will be prepared and issued by the Municipal Government.

Newly Established Ceremony The wedding ceremony has also been slightly changed, such as the officiant taking his seat, (4) the master of ceremonies leading the married persons to take their seats in turn (the seating arrangement in the auditorium stipulates that the officiant is in the center front, the last row on the left is the relatives, the female host and related persons are in the middle row, all married women are in the front row, the guests are in the last row on the left, the male and female hosts and related persons are in the middle row, all married men are in the front row, (5) performing the collective wedding ceremony, the married persons stand opposite each other to perform the wedding ceremony, (6) the married persons issue marriage certificates, the male and female hosts lead the male and female married persons in turn to receive them, and then return to their original positions (7) the officiant delivers a speech, (8) the ceremony is completed, the male and female married persons each leave with their arms crossed, the banquet after the wedding is: (1) After the wedding ceremony, the officiant invites all married persons to a banquet for celebration, and to wish for the beginning of a new life, (2) the married persons should take their seats according to the arranged seats, (3) After the banquet, the collective wedding ceremony is completed.

Marriage Instructions (1) Men and women who apply to participate in marriage must bring two recent full-body four-inch photos and stamps to the Public Welfare Section of the Bureau of Social Affairs to fill out the application form and pay the marriage fee of 20 yuan, which will be refunded if not approved. (2) After the application form is approved by the Bureau of Social Affairs, the male and female hosts must bring the introducer, the male and female married persons to the Bureau of Social Affairs to stamp on the marriage certificate within five days. (3) The male and female married persons must wear formal attire when they get married. (4) The male and female married persons must arrive at the Municipal Government at 1:30 pm on the wedding day and be led by the ceremony committee to the lounge to prepare for the ceremony. (5) The wedding time is scheduled for 3:00 pm. (6) No bridesmaids are allowed, but if the bride uses light gauze, she may bring children to hold the gauze, but no more than two. (7) The male and female married persons only need to bring two flower baskets themselves, and everything else does not need to be brought. Also, it is not allowed to scatter paper flowers and other items in the auditorium. (8) The male and female married persons will be invited to a banquet by the mayor, director, and their wives, and will be seated according to law. The hosts, introducers, and relatives will not prepare dishes on their behalf.

Wireless Engineering School Receives Machinery Donated by Jianghai Customs 162

Several patrol boats of the Jianghai Customs were equipped with spark-type radio transceivers. They have recently been retrofitted with new machines, and the old machines have been dismantled. Therefore, the Jianghai Customs Supervisory Office transferred these machines to the China Radio Engineering School on Avenue Edward VII in Shanghai. The school sent personnel on the 3rd of this month to receive them from the Pudong Machine Factory and Lanlu Branch of the Jianghai Customs. The items include spark gap transmitters, high-power transformers, motor starters, high-voltage capacitors, rotary converters, emergency circuit breakers, and various parts for the school's display and research purposes. The China Radio Engineering School has been established for a long time and is known for its serious management, strict curriculum, perfect equipment, and innovative instruments. Its past achievements have earned considerable reputation in the country. Thousands of graduates have been employed in public and private transportation agencies. In the recent year, most of the radio operators employed by the Customs have been graduates of the school. It is reported that the school's next enrollment will be on January 6th and 13th of next year, and the opening date will be January 15th.

Emergency Relief Universal Donation Movement Enthusiastically Supported by Industrial and Commercial Circles 164

General Labor Union and Municipal Chamber of Commerce Both Issue Notices

Since the start of the emergency relief universal donation movement in the city, the work has been quite intense in recent days. Tomorrow is "Workers' Donation" Day. In addition to submitting a request to the municipal government to order the employers of all factories to deduct one day's wages for relief, and notifying all labor unions to instruct all workers to comply, in accordance with the resolution of the Temporary Representative Conference, the Municipal General Labor Union has also issued a letter to all workers in the city, excerpted below:

Letter to the Workers Dear workers of the city, in the past two years, industry and commerce in the city have been declining, the market has been depressed, and factories have been closing down and reducing work hours. Unemployed workers are increasing, and the lives of workers in the city are extremely difficult. The reason for this is the impact of the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, but the unrest caused by the communists in the interior, the lack of livelihood, the bankruptcy of rural areas, and the reduction of purchasing power, resulting in the stagnation of cargo transportation and the sluggish sales, are the biggest reasons. This year, various provinces have suffered from severe drought, affecting eleven provinces and tens of millions of victims. The cries of distress spread everywhere, and refugees are fleeing, making the situation even more difficult to describe. Under such circumstances of communist disasters, droughts, and floods, the compatriots in the disaster areas are already on the verge of death, and the productive and purchasing power have been lost. As a result, the industry and commerce of the city are becoming increasingly weak. Mayor Wu Tiecheng has initiated a major emergency relief universal donation movement to revive the disaster victims and stabilize the disaster areas. He has convened meetings with various agencies and important groups in the city to discuss the establishment of a donation committee for emergency relief to various disaster areas to actively carry out the work. At the same time, the General Labor Union also convened a meeting of representatives of various labor unions on the 5th to decide that all workers in the city should donate one day's wages, and piece-rate workers should donate 50 cents per person, to collect our blood and sweat to assist the government and various sectors of the city in completing this urgent disaster relief work. Dear workers, we have always been reluctant to lag behind in saving the country and other public welfare undertakings. Of course, we will not sit idly by in this major emergency relief universal donation movement. We must know that although our current lives are painful, it is nothing compared to the disaster-stricken compatriots who have no clothes or food. Therefore, it is our duty to donate one day's wages to help them. Furthermore, the compatriots in the disaster areas will stabilize their lives due to emergency relief and will be able to restore their productive power and purchasing power. Then, the industry and commerce of the city can return to prosperity, and our lives can also get a considerable turnaround. Therefore, this kind of emergency relief movement, although it is said to be saving people, can also be said to be saving ourselves. I hope that my dear workers will uphold the spirit of seeing justice and acting bravely and enthusiastically contribute.

Notice to Union Members The Municipal General Labor Union yesterday notified various labor unions in a document stating, for the purpose of notification, this year's severe drought has caused disasters everywhere, with crop failures, affecting eleven provinces and tens of millions of victims. The cries of distress spread everywhere, and refugees are fleeing, either digging up grass roots to satisfy their hunger or peeling bark to fill their stomachs. The scene is tragic and unbearable to witness. The compatriots in Jiangxi, Hunan, Fujian, and Anhui have suffered the ravages of the Red bandits, and wealthy families have become poor people, and the extremely poor households have turned into starving people. The severity of the disaster is even more difficult to describe. As the severe cold is approaching, the disaster victims have no clothes or food. If they are not rescued quickly, they will fill the gullies. Therefore, Mayor Wu Tiecheng of the city has initiated a major emergency relief universal donation movement and has established the "Shanghai Emergency Relief Universal Donation Committee for Disaster Areas" to actively carry out the work. Comrades in the labor sector are brave in doing good and have never lagged behind. For this righteous act, how can we sit idly by? The union convened a temporary representative meeting of various labor unions on the 5th and decided that all workers in the city should donate one day's wages, and piece-rate workers should donate 50 cents per person for relief, and set the 10th as the Workers' Donation Day. In addition to requesting the municipal government to order the employers of all factories to deduct the wages and remit them to the Shanghai Bank, this notice is to inform the union to immediately inform all workers to comply, to be happy to support, and to jointly promote this righteous act. This is extremely important. Attending members: Zhu Xuefan, Standing Committee members: Zhou Xuexiang, Li Mengnan, Ye Xianggao, Shao Xubai, Long Peiyun.

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce issued a public notice yesterday for soliciting emergency relief for disaster areas in various provinces, and notified various industry associations to convene meetings to deliberate on fundraising. The original text is as follows:

Public Notice to the Business Community The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce is issuing a public notice to the business community on the matter of requesting the business community to raise funds to help disaster areas in various provinces, stating that the Municipal Emergency Relief Universal Donation Committee for Disaster Areas has sent a letter stating that the disaster situation in various provinces this year is extremely severe and has requested to consult with various industries on the method of emergency relief universal donation. As the severe winter is approaching, disaster victims in various provinces lack clothing and food. Fundraising for emergency relief is urgently needed. In addition, this year's disaster area is vast and unique. It is necessary to gather all strengths and efforts to ensure more comprehensive protection. Although the Shanghai market is in a state of commercial depression, it is a safe area. It is requested that all sectors of the city's business community enthusiastically donate to the best of their ability. This is of utmost importance. In addition to notifying various industries separately, it is feared that there will be omissions. Therefore, it is hereby republished in the newspaper for public notice.

Notice to Various Industries Received a letter from the Municipal Emergency Relief Universal Donation Committee for Disaster Areas stating that this year's water and drought disasters have spread to various provinces, the disaster area is vast, the disaster situation is severe, and there are few such cases. The Shanghai market is in a time of commercial depression, but those who are hungry and drowning are all compatriots who cannot control themselves. If they can each do their part, accumulate small amounts to make a large amount, it will be beneficial to the overall situation of relief. Small Port Steamer Company Opposes Joint Road-Water Transportation 165

Tonghua's Maiden Voyage Today

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has newly opened a joint transportation route connecting Lianyungang and Qingdao, scheduled to commence today with the dispatch of the Tonghua vessel on its maiden voyage. Unexpectedly, this has ignited a wave of opposition from all shipping merchants and customs brokers of the small ports, who have telegraphed to the Ministries of Communications and Railways, requesting a halt. However, both the road and water transportation parties believe that the joint operation will not hinder the business of commercial steamers and are proceeding as planned. Detailed information is as follows:

The Tonghua's voyage to Lianyungang, Laoyao, and Qingdao has traditionally been serviced by over twenty vessels dispatched by the small port steamer companies in that area. These vessels travel from Dapu to Qingdao, passing through ports such as Shijiusuo, Shidao, Lidiao, Chenjia Village, Wangjiatan, Zhucun, Lanshantou, Zhewan, Xiangshui River Mouth, and Qingkou. Their business encompasses both cargo and passenger transport. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's joint operation involves a direct route from Laoyao to Qingdao, bypassing the small ports, thus reaching the destination in only ten hours. The Tonghua vessel has been designated to exclusively operate this line, commencing its maiden voyage from Shanghai today.

Original Steamers for Small Ports: On this route, there are, including Changji's Changchun, Yingchun, Dechun, Tongchun; Fulohang's Yuantai, Hengtai, Litai, Shixiang; Yihua's Tongxing, Yongxiang, Yuchang Second; Yingji's Xinshun; Shandong Shangyun's Qinghai; Litong's Hengtong, Haitong; Yitong, Yiyuangong's Liji, Liyi; Nakamura Group's Qingxing, Maosheng, totaling twenty-four vessels. Even more sailboats are engaged in cargo transport. Ordinarily, their business heavily relies on freight from the Longhai Railway.

United Opposition: Customs brokers in the Dapu area, who rely on small port steamer transportation for cargo, including Dechangtai, Yongfeng, Changlong, Huifeng, Heyi, Changren, Huaji, and forty-one others, have already voiced their opposition when ships called at Laoyao. With the opening of the Lianyungang-Qingdao route, the small port steamer companies, united with the customs brokers, are collectively resisting, having petitioned the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways to stop it, in order to maintain the small port shipping business and prevent thousands from becoming unemployed.

Road and Water Transportation Disregard: The Longhai Railway's preparations for the opening of the new Lianyungang-Qingdao route are reportedly complete. Construction at the Laoyao wharf is finished, allowing for the berthing of one more vessel. Starting from December, an additional 130 railway police officers will be assigned to handle the loading and unloading of cargo for this route. They have resolved to ignore the opposition from the small port steamer customs brokers, arguing that the routes are different, with one serving Dapu and the other sailing to Laoyao. Furthermore, the Tonghua vessel will not call at the various ports, minimizing conflict. However, to protect the business of the small port steamers, the road and water transportation parties have adopted a non-competitive approach, setting the freight rate at three yuan per ton, maintaining the same price level.

Ministry of Communications Dispatches Personnel to England to Supervise Telephone Equipment Manufacturing 168

Qian Qishen and Others Scheduled to Go Abroad

The Ministry of Communications is planning to establish long-distance telephone service in nine provinces, and various telephone equipment and cables have been ordered in England, as previously reported. It is now learned that the Ministry of Communications has determined that it is imperative to send personnel to supervise the manufacturing of the telephone equipment and cables, in order to ensure that the equipment can be used to improve the efficiency of the telephone system after it is shipped back to China. Specifically, Qian Qishen, a technical specialist, Niu Yinchu, director of the Suzhou Telephone Bureau, and technicians Sun Zheng and Huang Ruzu have been dispatched to England for supervision. After the completion of the telephone equipment and cables, technicians Sun Zheng and Huang Ruzu will bring them back first, while Qian (as he referred to himself) and Niu will then go to Germany, France, and other countries to study telephone management operations. They are expected to return to China by the end of next year. They are currently preparing for their journey and are scheduled to set sail on the Devanha on the 11th.

Shanghai Municipal Council Bond Conversion 169

1924 Bonds Converted to 1934 Bonds

The Shanghai Municipal Council, in accordance with the resolution of the Taxpayers' Annual Meeting on April 18 of this year, announced that it would raise funds not exceeding 15.5 million yuan within this year. It now announces that the 1924 silver tael bonds (totaling 5 million taels), which are due for redemption, will be converted to 1934 silver dollar bonds. The conversion procedure offers favorable terms to bondholders and will not affect the financial market. The conversion rate is calculated at 7 mace 1.5 li of silver per yuan. The new bonds are in Shanghai's standard national currency, with an annual interest rate of 5%, payable on June 30 and December 31 each year, with the first payment due on June 30 of next year.

The new bonds are issued at par value and are scheduled to be redeemed at par value on December 31, 1964. However, the Municipal Council may redeem part or all of the bonds by the end of 1944, and may also redeem them at any time thereafter, provided that six months' prior notice is published in Shanghai. If only part of the bonds are to be redeemed, the bond numbers to be redeemed will be determined by lottery.

The bonds are secured by the Municipal Council's real estate and annual tax revenues. However, the 1925, 1926, and 1927 bonds have priority of redemption. A fund has been prepared for these old bonds, which should be fully redeemed by the end of 1937.

The new bonds are available in denominations of 10,000 yuan, 5,000 yuan, 1,000 yuan, 500 yuan, and 100 yuan. Bondholders of the already registered 1924 bonds have already received conversion forms from the Municipal Council. The forms must be completed and submitted to the Chief Accountant of the Municipal Council no later than the 24th of this month for conversion.
