Li Zhiming, Who Stabbed His Cousin-in-Law to Death, Sentenced to Life Imprisonment 171

Declares in Court That He Will Not Accept the Sentence if Not Executed

Li Zhiming, a local resident of Zhoujiaqiao in western Shanghai, is only twenty-two years old. He studied at Jingye School in this city in his early years. After dropping out of school, he had no legitimate occupation and spent his days with a group of idle individuals. He became infected with bad habits. He sold his ancestral property one after another, spending the proceeds. According to Li, his cousin-in-law, Yao Minggao, had acted as an intermediary in the sale of soil from his land, secretly embezzling a portion of the money. Li was ignored when he confronted Yao. Filled with resentment, he gathered accomplices at night and broke into Yao's house, stabbing Yao's wife, Yao Lu, to death. Yao himself suffered more than a dozen knife wounds but fortunately was not killed. After the incident was discovered, Li Zhiming was arrested and sent to the Procuratorate of the District Court, where he confessed to the crime. He was prosecuted in the Criminal Court on charges of murder. Presiding Judge Sun Jikang conducted a public trial. As the case was clear, it was considered closed and awaiting sentencing, as previously reported. It is now learned that this case was publicly sentenced by Presiding Judge Sun Jikang in the Fifth Court yesterday morning. Li Zhiming was brought to the court and briefly questioned. The court sentenced the defendant to two sentences: one to fifteen years of imprisonment and the other to life imprisonment, to be executed as life imprisonment. After the sentence was pronounced, the judge asked: "If you do not accept the judgment, you can appeal according to the law." The defendant Li replied: "Why not execute me by shooting?" The judge said: "The crime you committed does not warrant execution by shooting." The defendant Li said: "If I am executed by shooting, I will accept the judgment. But I absolutely do not accept life imprisonment." The judge said: "You must submit your reasons within ten days and appeal according to the law." After the order was given, the defendant Li was returned to custody pending further instructions.

Tenants of Cianli Appeal Over Lease Contracts 172

- Second Special Court Scheduled to Hear Case on the 12th -

Tenants of houses in Cianli, Route Lafayette, French Concession, are deeply dissatisfied with the harsh contracts imposed by the Huizhong Real Estate Company, which they believe are designed to increase rents. Sixteen households, including the Tan, Chen, Wang, and Zhang families, have been forced to sign these contracts. They argue that the contracts were not established through legal methods and were not uniformly implemented for all tenants, and therefore are fundamentally invalid. They are determined to continue to fight for their rights. They have hired lawyers You Zhi and Li Ming to file a lawsuit in the Second Special District Court against the managers, Wang Xingyuan and Wang Zhiren. The hearing is currently scheduled for the 12th of this month.

Inspection Report of the China Agricultural Development Bank 178

The report on the inspection of the preparation for the issuance of notes by the China Agricultural Development Bank states that the bank's issuance reserve and operating reserve have always been completely separate. According to the bank's articles of association, the cash reserve should be above 70% and the guarantee reserve should be below 30%. On the 8th of this month, accountant Wang Zikang, together with Xu Guorong and Xu Busun, representatives of the board of directors and supervisors, conducted an inspection. The results were as follows: The total amount of banknotes issued was 7,084,000 silver dollars. The silver dollar reserve for exchange was 5,208,700 silver dollars, and the guarantee reserve was above 1,797,000 silver dollars. The cash reserve was above 70%, and the guarantee reserve was below 30%. This is a special report. 23/32.8

Shanghai National Products Company Winter Sale 179

The Shanghai National Products Company, located across from the Rainbow Temple on Nanjing Road, began its winter sale yesterday. All departments are offering special discounts to promote national products. The silk and satin department is even selling men's and women's funeral fabrics at cost. The more than 40 other departments, including cotton fabrics, leather goods, textiles, and knitwear, are offering bargains on all items. In addition, in order to promote the New Life Movement, a New Life Recreation Department has been set up on the second floor, offering table-top improved golf balls. Customers who purchase goods worth two yuan can play one ball. Those who can hit the four characters "Propriety, Justice, Integrity, Shame" in a row will be awarded a complete antelope fur robe or fox-lined coat worth nearly a hundred gold pieces. There are a total of 25 characters in the tray. Those who can hit a complete phrase will also be awarded prizes. Even those who hit one character will receive a good gift, ensuring that everyone receives a prize and is happy. Consequently, ladies from all walks of life flocked to purchase, creating an unusually crowded scene.

Zhabei Public Bus Changes the Value of Subsidiary Currency for Copper Coins 180

The Shanghai Chinese Public Bus Company's fares are based on copper coins. Paying with subsidiary currency, such as dime coins, was set at 44 copper coins for a double dime and 28 copper coins for a single dime banknote. However, recently the price of copper coins has risen, exceeding the above rates. It is said that in order to be fair to passengers paying with subsidiary currency on the bus, the company is temporarily referring to the subsidiary currency rates of the concession trams, i.e., 42 copper coins for a double dime and 29 copper coins for a single dime banknote. This will take effect on the 10th of this month. Once the price of copper coins returns to normal, the old rates will be used for exchange.

Education News

Second Day of the National Vocational Education Conference 185

Resolved to Rectify Vocational Schools in Provinces and Cities and Find Ways to Expand

Implement Agricultural Education Subsidies for Vocational Schools to Train Teachers

- The Conference Will Close This Morning After a General Meeting -

Two Groups Examining in the Morning 186

(Nanjing, 8th) The National Vocational Education Conference continued at the Ministry of Education at 9:00 AM on the 8th. In the morning, the conference divided into two groups for examination. One was the Vocational Education Funding Allocation Standards Examination Committee, and the other was the Vocational School Department Establishment and Graduate Employment Issues Examination Committee. The above two examination committees completed the examination of each case and submitted them to the general meeting for discussion.

Second General Meeting in the Afternoon 187

At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, the second general meeting was held. The attendees were the same as yesterday. Gu Shusheng, chairman, reported the examination opinions on the standards for the allocation of vocational school funding, and the meeting then entered into discussion.

1. Regarding how each province and city should realize the Ministry-designated standards for the establishment and funding allocation of secondary schools, the meeting resolved to adopt the original plan. The word "how" in items 1, 2, and 3 was deleted, and the following was added: 4. If any province or city has special difficulties and the Ministry of Education confirms that this is the case, the deadline for completing the standards may be extended, but only for one or two years. 5. When provinces and cities realize the Ministry-designated standards, the Ministry of Education will verify the extent to which they have been achieved or the special difficulties, and provide subsidies as appropriate. 6. The Ministry of Education is requested to suggest that the central government allocate 3 million to 5 million yuan annually from fiscal year 24 (1935) onwards for the purpose of subsidizing vocational education in the provinces and cities.

2. Regarding how each province and city should, based on the industrial situation and the types of vocational talent needed in their province and city, reorganize the department establishment of existing vocational schools and determine the types of departments to be established in future vocational schools, the meeting resolved: 1. Each province and city should quickly establish a vocational education design committee, responsible for investigation, contact, and research. Its tasks are as follows: 1. Investigate the industrial situation, vocational types, and talent needs of each industry in the province or city. 2. Conduct a detailed investigation of the department establishment of existing public and private vocational schools in each province and city, to determine whether there are any shortcomings, whether they correspond to the needs, and whether employment is convenient for graduates from each department. Departments that do not correspond to the needs should be subject to reasonable control and reorganized into other departments. 3. Formulate specific plans for the addition of departments in future public and private vocational schools and implement them in stages. 4. Each province and city should formulate the following three standards for designing the promotion of vocational education: 1. Establish more vocational supplementary schools and junior vocational schools. 2. Senior vocational schools should focus on graduation. 3. Restrictions should be placed on the establishment of commercial vocations.

3. The temporary proposal by Jiang Hengyuan, Zheng Xigu, Lai Zhizhong, Zheng Tan, Miao Ying, and Lu Dianyang to promote agricultural education, including the proposal from Henan Province to improve agricultural education in China, the proposal from Fujian Province to request each province and city to pay special attention to agricultural teaching and practice for rural teachers and rural primary schools as a subsidy for the promotion of agricultural education, and the proposal from Sichuan Province to request the Ministry of Education to order each province and city to establish agricultural instructor training classes as soon as possible to help the countryside and increase production, were merged for discussion and resolved: Please revise and pass the proposal by Jiang Hengyuan and others.

4. (4) Senior vocational school students have many seasonal internship problems, and concentrated military training is difficult. It is proposed to exempt them. This case was temporarily proposed for discussion by Lu Dianyang and other representatives from 25 provinces and cities. The resolution was: 1. Senior vocational first-year students are directly exempted from centralized military training. 2. After the centralized military training is exempted, the peacetime military training will be extended to the second grade, with one year to make up for the time. 3. For the above two points, please consult with the General Supervision Department of Training for approval and implementation.

5. (5) Each province and city should quickly reorganize or enrich the original vocational schools and ban substandard public and private vocational schools. Amended and passed.

6. (6) The central and each province and city should subsidize excellent public and private vocational schools. Amended and passed.

7. (7) Train vocational school teachers. Amended and passed. The meeting adjourned at 5:30.

Outline of Jiang Wenyu's Speech 188

The Meaning and Function of Vocational Guidance

At 5:00 PM on the 7th, the vocational education discussion meeting invited Jiang Wenyu to speak on the meaning and function of vocational guidance. The outline of his speech is as follows: 1. The Definition of Vocational Guidance: (1) The definition stipulated by the National Vocational Guidance Association of the United States: Vocational guidance is to provide facts, experience, and opinions to help individuals choose a profession, prepare for a profession, obtain a profession, and improve a profession. (2) The slogan set by the Chinese Vocational Education Society: "To enable the unemployed to have a job, and those who have a job to enjoy their work." 2. The Origin and Development of Vocational Guidance: (1) In China. (2) In Europe. (3) In the United States. (4) In Japan. 3. The Nature and Function of Vocational Guidance: (1) Universal social need. (2) Long-term maintenance. (3) Cooperation with others. (4) Only assisting people and not making decisions for them. (5) Examination of both the individual and society. 4. The Scope and Effectiveness of Vocational Guidance: (1) Individual: Youth, Adults. (2) Social: Vocations, Families. (3) Schools: Ordinary primary and secondary schools, vocational schools, universities, and specialized vocational supplementary schools, other training institutions. 5. Steps of Vocational Guidance: (1) Separate investigation. (2) Providing methods, imparting knowledge. (3) Examination of personal performance. (4) Equipment, forms, instruments, further education, career choice, career change, all other personnel matters. (5) Introducing vocations. (6) Improving vocations. 6. Implementation of Vocational Guidance: (1) Establishing institutions, guidance institutions, implementing institutions. (2) Training talent. (3) Statistics, research, editing, reporting.

Third General Meeting This Morning 189

The third general meeting will continue at 8:00 AM on the 9th. First, He Qingru will be invited to speak on the scientific methods of vocational guidance. If all the cases are discussed in the morning, the meeting will be closed at noon. Otherwise, the fourth meeting will continue in the afternoon before closing.

Zhejiang Education Bureau Divides into Three Regions for This Year's Middle School Graduation Joint Examination 195

Examination areas are divided into Hangzhou, Jinhua, and Taizhou

A total of thirty high schools and middle schools participate in the joint examination

The Zhejiang Education Bureau has determined that the first semester middle school graduation joint examination for the 23rd year is approaching, and the examination area has been divided into three regions: Hangzhou, Jinhua, and Taizhou, to be held separately. The examination venue for the Hangzhou region is at the Provincial Hangzhou High School, the examination venue for the Jinhua region is at the Provincial Jinhua Middle School, and the examination venue for the Taizhou region is at the Haimen Third District Party Department. It is reported that this year, one high school and thirty middle schools are approved for the joint examination and have graduating classes. The Education Bureau has already notified all participating schools of the joint examination method in separate regions. The Education Bureau has also stipulated that students who failed the joint examination in previous years should participate in the supplementary examination for high school students in the Hangzhou region, and middle school students should participate in the supplementary examination in one of the three regions they have determined. However, once a region is determined, they may not apply to transfer to another region. In addition, students who took the supplementary examination in the third and fourth sessions must first take the school graduation examination for the subjects they passed and submit the grade report for review. If they have transferred to another school, the original school should set the questions and entrust the school where they are studying to conduct the graduation examination and submit the grade report for review. This supplementary examination method has also been ordered to all schools to comply with.

Sports News

Upsets in the Sko-Ta Cup 198

Lax eliminates West Point 1-0

Chinese Point also defeats West Commerce 1-0

Today, Yu You plays French Commerce at the Yiyuan

In the second week of the Sko-Ta Cup, Donghua first defeated Inness 5-0. Both games yesterday were upsets. (1) Lax defeated West Point 1-0. (2) Chinese Point also eliminated West Commerce 1-0, which was unexpected. Today, there is another game between Yu You and French Commerce, held at the Yiyuan. After this game, it will be the quarter-finals week. This year, the Chinese team has high hopes for the championship.

Chinese Point Actually Defeats Southwest Commerce 199

The battle between Chinese Point and Southwest Commerce was held at the Yiyuan. The performance of both teams was mediocre and uninteresting. Southwest Commerce is getting worse and worse, and its military appearance is declining. It was actually defeated by Chinese Point 1-0, causing 2,000-3,000 spectators to cheer and rejoice beyond expectation. Chinese Point goalkeeper Yin Xingsheng was very lucky and saved countless dangerous balls, which was a great contribution to Chinese Point. The lineups of the two teams are as follows:

Chinese Point

Yin Xingsheng, Ma Bingzhang, Xue Zhiwen, Zhu Guiquan, Miao Huaguo, Zhang Ziquan, Wu Xiquan, Liao Zhonggan, Dong Zhaobin, Qiu Tiansheng, Yao Jiagui

Southwest

Lewis, McLaughlan, Faping, Beeches, Stokes, Haite, Leif, Los, McCaughan, Tal, Fasde, Columba, Larson

Southwest Commerce's Luck is Really Bad Isn't Southwest Commerce really not as good as Chinese Point? In short, it's just bad luck. From beginning to end, Chinese Point was in a position of being oppressed, and Southwest Commerce attacked frequently, but could not find its way in. In fact, Chinese Point was on the big stage for the first time, and everyone was full of energy and morale. They also focused on defense with all their strength, so that Southwest Commerce had no way to use its strength, and could only lament helplessly.

Yao Jiagui Opens the Record The first half passed peacefully, and neither side gained anything. About ten minutes after the start of the second half, Chinese Point suddenly broke free from its imprisoned state. Qiu Tiansheng sent a ball flying forward. Dong Zhaobin took advantage of the emptiness inside the opponent, and moved forward one step, passing the ball left and right. About twenty-five yards from the goal, he suddenly kicked the ball, with great force. The ball rebounded from the crossbar of the goal. The goalkeeper was shocked. Chinese Point's right winger Yao Jiagui had just rushed to the side of the goal and saw the ball kick it with one foot, and the ball flew into the goal. It bounced down from the crossbar and had passed the goal line. The goalkeeper hurriedly patted it with his hand, but it was too late.

Yin Xingsheng Protects the Country With Merit Chinese Point's victory was like a joy from the sky, and their morale was even more boosted. Wu Xiquan had two passes, and the landing points were excellent, but unfortunately the players in the middle did not respond properly and missed the opportunity. Southwest Commerce was unwilling to show weakness and launched a full counterattack, shooting furiously in succession. However, their luck was not good, either going out of bounds or hitting the crossbar. Moreover, goalkeeper Yin Xingsheng was blessed with inspiration and saved countless dangerous balls, earning thunderous applause. The country was preserved, and a victory song was sung, which was all thanks to this gentleman. After the game, he came out of the field and was surrounded by the audience and was very popular.

Lax Defeats West Point 200

Another Sko-Ta Cup game was between Lax and West Point, which clashed at the Racecourse. Westerners watched, surrounded like a wall. West Point's strength has always been known as fierce. Lax was originally a fierce general, but before the game, it was generally speculated that West Point would not have difficulty winning. Unexpectedly, the result was the opposite. Lax eliminated West Point 1-0. This ball was scored by Bauselier in the first half. The competition between the two teams was fierce and the performance was quite good. The depression of Western teams in fact gives Yu You great hope in China.

Today, Yu You Fights French Commerce 201

There is still one game in the second week of the Sko-Ta Cup, which is between French Commerce and Yu You. They will meet at Yiyuan at 3 pm. In last week's United game, Yu You defeated French Commerce 5-3. Today, they meet again on a narrow road, and there will be an even more fierce competition. Moreover, after West Point lost to Lax and West Commerce lost to Chinese Point yesterday, the Chinese team has a great influence. I hope Yu You will work hard for it. If Yu You also loses to French Commerce, then in the future quarter-finals, the Western team will only have one Lax, and the Chinese team will occupy three. The championship will belong to the Chinese team.

Donghua Football Team Leaves for Beijing This Morning 202

Total Distance: Five and Six-Tenths Miles

The Pegasus Cross-Country Team, established for six years, has a long history and is a leading team in Shanghai. Recognizing past failures in international competitions, the team is determined to avenge them. Therefore, they are holding a cross-country race in the downtown area, divided into team and individual categories. The starting point is at the front gate of Fudan University, and the finish line is in front of the university's gymnasium. The total distance is five and six-tenths miles. The team considers this competition a pioneering event in Shanghai's sports scene. Therefore, all procedures are being handled with utmost care to avoid negligence. They hope that outstanding athletes in Shanghai's sports community will participate in this event.

The route starts from the front gate of Fudan University, proceeds along Xiangyin Road, turns onto Songhu Road, Sanmin Road, and Fuxi Inner Road, passes in front of the Municipal Government, enters Fuxian Left Road, Funan Left Road, Xiangyin Road, and returns to the finish line in front of the Fudan University Gymnasium, covering approximately five and six-tenths miles.

The competition will be held in two stages: (A) The team competition will be held at 10:00 AM on the 16th of this month; (B) The individual competition will be held at 10:00 AM on the 23rd of this month.

Scoring: (A) Each team in the team competition must have at least six and up to ten participants. The scores of the top six members will be counted, and the team with the lowest score will be the champion. (B) In the individual competition, the ranking will be based solely on the order of finish.

Prizes: For general participation, the top 20% will receive awards. In addition to silver championship trophies for the champion team and individual, each participant will receive a commemorative medal.

Registration: Registration is open from now until the 13th of this month at the following locations: (A) Fudan University Sports Department; (B) Chinese Single-Sport Athletics Promotion Association (272 Daji Road, Nanshi); (C) Liangyou Sporting Goods Company (567 Bazhi Road, near North Henan Road); (D) Jin Lu, Fudan University Pegasus Cross-Country Team (for mail-in registration only; please register by certified mail to avoid loss; the team is not responsible for lost mail). The entry fee is two yuan per team for bib numbers and pins, and twenty cents per person.

Athlete Notes: (A) Athletes who are more than 15 minutes late will be considered to have forfeited. (B) Bib numbers must be attached to both the front and back of the chest, with all four corners securely pinned. Failure to do so will result in disqualification from the competition. (C) The route will be marked with lime lines and Boy Scout guides. Athletes must not run on the sidewalk, take shortcuts, or push other competitors.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Why "Silence"? 214

— Xuanzi

Every Monday morning, you all have the Commemoration Week, and after reading the Premier's Will, you follow it with "three minutes of silence." What exactly does this "silence" mean? Some of you children may not really know, and during the "silence," you might even be whispering. Some of you may even complain that the "silence" is too long, which is all wrong.

You read the Will and are required to "be silent" precisely so that you can remember the Premier in silence and think carefully about whether you have fulfilled every sentence in the Premier's Will. If you haven't, how should we, with a spirit of perseverance, continue the Premier's spirit to carry out the instructions he left us?

Only by doing so can we be true followers of the Premier, and this is something that all you children must remember.

Childhoods of World Celebrities 215

— Yin

Lincoln

Have you, friends, heard of Lincoln, the famous American president who liberated black slaves, prohibited slaveholding, and advocated humanitarianism? When he was a child, his family was very poor. They didn't have enough to eat, and they lived in a dilapidated wooden house built from planks. He naturally had no opportunity to study. He only attended primary school for six months. After he learned some characters, he studied hard on his own. He helped his father with work and studied at the same time. He didn't have money to buy books, so he borrowed them from friends he knew.

Once, he read a biography of Washington and learned about Washington's character. He suddenly slammed the book and shouted, "I will be like Washington in the future!" Those who heard him say this laughed at him and looked down on him because even the clothes he wore were very worn out. How could he ever become such a great figure?

But, children, do you believe it? The success of a great cause does not depend on having money, but on having a spirit of perseverance, a strong will, and also on having chivalrous behavior. Lincoln had all of these. One day, he saw a drunkard fall into a ditch. He helped him up and took him to a nearby house, asking the owner to let him sleep there. He personally took care of him until he woke up. At this time, he was only a twelve or thirteen-year-old child. Children, look at Lincoln's behavior in his childhood. How brave and righteous!

Honesty was also Lincoln's behavior when he was a child. When he was eighteen, he helped out as a clerk in a shop. In a hurry, he overcharged a customer four pence (a British currency). When he was balancing the accounts in the evening, he remembered it. He took the money to the customer's house. The road was long, and it was late at night, but Lincoln didn't care about that. He felt that integrity was more important than anything else!

Lincoln's spirit, will, and behavior in his childhood ultimately led to his great achievements when he grew up. Children, what are your thoughts after reading this story?

Don't Be Afraid of the Cold 216

— A Duo

Children! Winter is here again! Although winter is cold, we should still pay attention to hygiene as usual.

There are many things that everyone doesn't do because they are afraid of the cold! So I'm here to remind you:

Do not close the windows at night to prevent poor air circulation.

Do not cover your head with the blanket when sleeping; sleeping with your head covered is unhygienic.

Be careful when walking if you are wearing too many clothes.

Don't take off your clothes immediately after exercising and getting hot, as you may catch a cold.

Winter games: Do not play with water, do not play with fire; playing with water will freeze your hands, playing with fire is dangerous.

Table Salt 217

— Zhen

Children, have you studied chemistry? Children who have studied it will definitely say it's difficult, but chemistry is very interesting.

Children, do you know how table salt is made?

(1) Solar evaporation: In coastal areas, salt fields are set up on the coast. When the tide rises, seawater is directed into the salt fields. The power of the wind and the heat of the sun are used to evaporate the water. When the solution reaches the appropriate concentration, it is poured into a crystallization pond to crystallize into table salt.

(2) Boiling: Seawater is directed into salt fields, which are covered with fine sand. Because fine sand can absorb water, sunlight and wind are used to evaporate the water. After sunset, the sand is piled up. The next day, the sand is spread out again, and seawater is poured in, then dried and piled again. After several days of this, when the salt content in the sand reaches the appropriate concentration, the sand is placed in a cabinet-shaped filter, and seawater is poured in to dissolve the salt and filter it out, separating it from the mud and sand. This highly concentrated filtrate is placed in a pot and dried to obtain table salt.

If table salt is dissolved into a solution and electrolyzed, positive and negative electrodes are passed through it. As a result, a yellow-green gas is produced on one side, which is chlorine, a very poisonous gas. On the other side, a gray metallic solid is produced, which is sodium. If sodium is placed in water, it is very dangerous, and sodium cannot be held in the hand.

Children, I think you believe that chlorine and sodium are both very poisonous things. Wouldn't eating them be deadly?

Table salt is not poisonous at all because table salt is a compound of chlorine and sodium, so it is also called sodium chloride, and it has lost the original properties of chlorine and sodium.

Winter Knowledge 218

— Qian Chuohengjiu

(1) When the weather is very cold, water containers such as vases and water bowls often crack because the water inside freezes into ice, increasing its volume. If we want to prevent this problem, just dissolve some table salt in the water, and this problem will not occur. Because the salt solution can lower the freezing point of the water, it will not freeze easily.

(2) In winter, many people often get frostbite on their hands or feet, which is really a painful thing, but we also have ways to treat it; just add some hydrochloric acid to hot water and wash it, and it will get better in a few days.

Several Interesting Questions and Answers 219

— Yuntian

(1) Why do we feel hungry?

Answer: Our stomach is an organ composed entirely of muscles. The movement of this organ allows food to be digested. If our stomach has been empty for several hours, it will begin to undergo intermittent spasmodic contractions. At the same time as these contractions, we feel hunger. Therefore, the direct cause of hunger is the muscular contraction of the stomach.

(2) Why do we bend our bodies forward when going uphill? Why do we straighten our bodies when going downhill?

Answer: Our body's center of gravity is roughly at the waist. When going uphill, if we don't bend forward, our legs will move forward, and our center of gravity will lose its balance, and we will immediately fall back. The same principle applies to straightening the body when going downhill.

(3) Why does the weather get hot and cold?

Answer: Because the Earth rotates, sunlight strikes the Earth at an angle, and the heat is insufficient, so the weather gets cold in winter. If it strikes the Earth directly, it becomes hot. In addition, air convection can also cause changes in the climate.

(4) Why does touching iron feel colder than touching wood?

Answer: Iron conducts heat faster than wood. When you touch iron, the heat from your hand is transferred away more quickly, so it feels colder.

(5) Why can't we see things in a dark room?

Answer: All things that can enter a person's eyes rely on the reflection of light. There is no light in a dark room, so we can't see.

Kicking Shuttlecock 222

— Wang Shouqiu

Now, many children are enthusiastically kicking shuttlecock, because kicking shuttlecock is originally a form of entertainment in autumn and winter!

Children have very few noble and beneficial forms of entertainment. Only kicking shuttlecock can not only serve as a game, but also strengthen the body, so now there are many people advocating the sport of kicking shuttlecock. The method of making a shuttlecock is like this: use a goose feather tube, cut it into an inch long, put it inside a copper coin with a hole, and then wrap the copper coin with cloth along one end of the goose feather tube and sew it well with thread. Then find a few colorful chicken feathers with white down from the tail of a rooster and insert them into the goose feather tube, and a shuttlecock is made?

The way to kick a shuttlecock is even more varied and ingenious, with each person coming up with their own tricks. There is front kicking; there is back kicking; there is alternating kicking with two feet; there are those who kick the shuttlecock to their faces; there are even those who kick it onto their backs; and there are also those who use their noses to catch it; those who know how to kick can not only kick out many styles, but also can kick hundreds, thousands of times, and never let it fall on the ground. However, those who are just starting to kick can often only kick it two times; at most, they can kick it eight or ten times. So kicking shuttlecock also requires daily practice. Only then can you gradually increase the number of kicks, because kicking shuttlecock is also an art!

Children! If you don't kick much; if you don't kick well; you must not be impatient. You must know that those who kick a lot; those who kick well; have also practiced hard. You only need to keep kicking every day, and naturally one day you will kick a lot; you will kick well!

Animal Hibernation 223

— Bing Yu

When we reach winter, because the temperature of the external air goes up and down, the temperature of the blood also rises and falls with the climate. Cold-blooded animals such as reptiles and amphibians spend the winter by lowering their blood temperature, but the term "cold-blooded animal" does not actually mean that they are all cold-blooded. For example, if the temperature suddenly drops in winter, animals living in cold places will not hibernate if they are moved to tropical places. In cold places, the blood of cold-blooded animals gradually decreases with the temperature, the activity of cells becomes sluggish, the digestive power decreases, and all functions decline, so they don't want to eat or move and crawl on the ground. Generally, these cold-blooded animals will hibernate at temperatures below sixty degrees. When the temperature rises above sixty degrees after winter, they will become active again and want to eat. The same is true for animals in the water as it is on land. They sink to the bottom of the water and rely entirely on the respiration of their skin to get through the winter. For example, turtles sink to the bottom of the water and stop breathing completely, but they have already ingested a lot of food before hibernation, so they don't need to eat. If you feed them food randomly at this time, even if they eat it, they won't digest it and will excrete it in April or May, so there is no need to feed them during the hibernation period, as for raising them in a greenhouse, that is different.

Fan Wenzheng Gong 224

— Yan Shi

Children! Do you know the deeds of Fan Wenzheng Gong? He was a virtuous prime minister during the Northern Song Dynasty. "Wenzheng Gong" is his posthumous title. His name was "Zhongyan". When he was young, his family was very poor, but he was able to maintain a persevering ambition in a harsh environment, living in a Buddhist temple and studying diligently. As for food? He cooked porridge once and divided it into several meals. As for side dishes? He only ate some pickled vegetables.

Later, he passed the imperial examination and became a scholar, and he took the responsibility of the country to heart, and said: "I should be the first to worry about the world's troubles, and the last to enjoy the world's pleasures." When he was the prime minister of Emperor Renzong of Song, there was a Western Xia state that was very afraid of him and said: "Little Fan Laozi, has tens of thousands of soldiers in his belly." Therefore, they did not dare to invade China. He was able to govern the world very peacefully, which shows that he was a very responsible person.

In his later years, he also established a kind of righteous field, specializing in saving the poor widowers, widows, orphans and lonely people in the local area. Children! You should also learn to be like him!

The Diet of Animals Without Mouths 225

— Ri Zhao

Children, when you see this topic, you will definitely ask me strangely, how can animals without mouths eat? If you have studied natural science, I think you must know that the lowest animals are just one cell. That is the amoeba!

The amoeba is very much like candy, and it stretches very quickly, and it lives in water. It has no feet all over its body. When moving, a certain part of its body will naturally protrude; we usually call it "pseudopods". If the pseudopod is too short to move, it will stretch out another one.

When an amoeba wants to take food, it stretches out its only pseudopod and wraps around the two sides of the food, like we hold it in our hands to eat. At this time, the pseudopods gradually merge together, and the food is wrapped into the interior of its body. After the food is digested, it is excreted from its body to the outside. This is indeed a characteristic of lower animals.

Friends, if you want to see this strange animal, you must rely on the power of a microscope; the illustration on the left shows it eating food.

Empty Word Practice 226

"Must: can" Must study to be able to read.

"Although: but" Although I like to read the Children's Weekly, I often have things I don't understand.

"Because: so" Because I often take a bath, so I am very clean.

"Not only: but also" Not only need to eat rice, but also need to eat vegetables.

"Thought: unexpectedly" Everyone thought I could win first place in the race. Unexpectedly, I fell halfway.

"Never: how" I have never played truant. How can you say I was hiding at my aunt's house yesterday?

"Since: why" Since you have slept, why are you still dozing off?

Science Mr. Transforms Magic 227

— He Gongchao

Empty Bottle Extinguishes Candle

Science Mr. is on stage again. In his hand, he is holding a glass bottle and a candle holder with a candle inserted in it.

He lit the candle and placed the glass bottle next to the candle holder. He asked the children below the stage, "Children, who can blow out this candle?"

Several small hands below the stage were raised at the same time, and they shouted in unison, "I can! ... I can ..."

...

Science Mr. said: "But I won't let you use your mouth to blow, that's not special. I want you to use this bottle to extinguish the candle."

This restriction stumped many of the children. Use a bottle to put out the fire? This is something no one can do.

But Science Mr. unhurriedly picked up the glass bottle, put it to his mouth, and blew air into it hard. After blowing for a while, he quickly pressed down on the mouth of the bottle and asked the children:

"Now you know what's inside this bottle?"

Some children said: "There is still nothing inside."

Some children said: "There is already a gust of air inside."

Science Mr. said: "There is already compressed air in this bottle. We release this compressed air, and we can blow out the candle." As he spoke, he pointed the mouth of the bottle at the candle flame, and when he released his hand, the candle went out.

"The power of this compressed air is very great. We can use machines to compress the air, make its volume smaller, and become compressed air. We seal this compressed air in an iron cylinder, and when it is released, its volume expands and can launch torpedoes.

"If I don't blow the air inside the bottle towards the mouth of the bottle and there is no compression, then no matter what, I won't be able to blow out the candle."

Testing tools - empty bottle, candle holder, and one candle each.

Page 17

Women's Garden

"Strange" Theories 228

— Bi Yao

We are now in a great age of idle talk. I have never seen the so-called "pure conversation" of the ancients; what people talk about now mostly revolves around women. They talk about movie stars, dance queens, school beauties, pretty faces, socialites, noble ladies... They talk and talk and still it's not enough, so they write about them. Currently floating on the sea (of public opinion) is a kind of appetizer to the conversation, something called the "Non-Marriage League"; everyone is spreading their claims, and there have been many famous articles, depicting it vividly, with great relish, it's just a pity that no one has been able to find out who the members are.

Today, if a knowledgeable woman makes a "non-marriage" proposition out of injustice over an adultery case, that would of course be strange; but to not think, not reflect, and to find strangeness in the strange, that is the strangeness of society! In recent days, several newspaper reporters have interviewed many famous women, and all have said they know nothing about this matter; how could such a grand league become so mysterious? I don't intend to protect women, insisting that this is all baseless talk; but even if it were true, what falls upon us in society is only the responsibility of guiding and correcting, not of exaggerating and mocking. Because they have, after all, suffered the greatest oppression for thousands of years, and a little childishness is not a heinous crime.

If it turns out this is just a rumor, that's even stranger; it's often said that "people of Chu love rumors." The people of Chu in the twenty years of civil war should have died enough, but now they can still spread all over the coast, how numerous are the people of Chu? Talking always becomes rumors, rumors always involve women, and rumors about women spread quickly everywhere, isn't that strange?

In recent years, supernatural novels and supernatural movies have become a prevalent malady in society. I remember Wang Yuyang's poem on *Liaozhai Zhiyi*: "Let us speak of it recklessly, let us listen recklessly, rain like silk under the bean trellis and melon frame, I suppose they dislike human speech, and love to hear ghosts singing poems from autumn graves." There are countless things that should be said in human speech! But people must only talk about the strange; the chaos and decline of society can be imagined. However, those who love themselves will not act against themselves, and will not follow the tide. If someone proposes a "non-marriage league," it is a dazzlingly strange theory; if it is someone's fabrication, and then widely promoted, then it is even stranger; in short, they are not people who cultivate themselves well.

Everywhere in society, people are talking about ghosts, about the mysterious, about gods, about women with "sexual" stimulation, marriage, adultery, always unprincipled talk; serious matters are left to iron hooves and cannons to resolve, to bloody brains to handle. Everyone is immersed in strange actions and strange theories, absurd and ridiculous, in nonexistent illusions; this strange nation can easily be branded as unnecessary. In fact, imperialists will also call us unnecessary!

Dedicated to Women's Movement Groups 229

— Guo Zhenyi

Everyone knows that the reason why men and women cannot be truly equal is that the traditional ideas of patriarchal society have not been completely broken, and a truly equal system for men and women has not been established. Although this women's rights movement has not fundamentally solved the women's problems, it at least shows the enthusiasm of women's own struggle and resistance, especially at this time when women are being driven back to the home to be good wives and mothers.

The revision of Article 239 of the Criminal Law is only a superficial victory; in reality, we still need to unite the power of the masses and work together; for the general laboring women, we should give them great assistance with the spirit of the group. Therefore, requiring the formulation of a perfect labor law is also an important item in the women's rights movement.

The issue of female workers has already attracted the attention of most people, and the suffering of female workers has also aroused social sympathy. The government has formulated a new-style factory law based on the principles of protecting motherhood and equal pay for equal work, and it was clearly ordered to be promulgated and implemented in 1931, but regrettably, the factory owners requested an extension. Up to now, this law is nothing more than empty words on paper. Before a more perfect labor law is explicitly stipulated, the groups that bear the mission of the women's movement should continue to urge the government to force the factory owners to implement it effectively.

Now, the most important articles of the factory law concerning women are roughly appended below:

(1) Factories shall not employ men or women under the age of fourteen as workers...

(2) Male and female workers who are over fourteen but under sixteen years of age are child laborers, and child laborers only engage in light work.

(3) Child laborers and female workers shall not engage in handling explosive, flammable, or toxic substances, or other work that is harmful to public morals or dangerous.

(4) The actual working hours for adult workers shall be eight hours per day in principle. If it is necessary to extend the hours due to local conditions or the nature of the work, it may be set at ten hours.

(5) Child laborers shall not work more than eight hours per day.

(6) Child laborers shall not work between 7:00 PM and 6:00 AM the next morning.

(7) Female workers shall not work between 10:00 PM and 6:00 AM the next morning.

(8) Workers shall have a half-hour rest period after working continuously for five hours.

(9) Workers shall have one day of rest in every seven days.

(10) Equal pay shall be given for equal work of the same effect for both men and women.

(11) Female workers shall stop working for eight weeks before and after childbirth, and their wages shall be paid as usual.

(12) If a female worker stops working in accordance with the provisions of Article 37 of the Factory Law, a doctor's diagnosis certificate shall be obtained at the request of the factory.

(13) The work assignment of child laborers, female workers, and workers over the age of fifty shall be determined after a health examination.

(14) Factories employing female workers shall, to the extent possible, set up nurseries and employ nurses to take good care of them.

Thoughts on Visiting the "Ping Le" Women's Detention Center 230

— Qian

It was on an afternoon in early June, when the broad climate changed from slightly warm to extremely hot, that I visited the women's prison of the Ping Le Detention Center -- this women's prison is connected to the men's prison within the same courtyard. Not far from the entrance gate, there is a very large wooden fence, and in front of the ticket-selling-like desk outside the fence gate, sits a male prison staff member. On the desk, like a rockery, is a high pile of keys. On the side of the desk, there is a small uncovered box, filled with broken copper and scrap iron. According to the warden, Ms. Suo Zhang, who was acting as the guide, that is the foot shackles and handcuffs that the prisoners wear at night. Not far after entering the first fence gate is the second fence gate. At this time, the female prison staff member inside the fence gate, upon the introduction of Ms. Suo Zhang, immediately smiled and picked up her treasured possession -- a large string of keys of all sizes, and came to greet us. While we exchanged greetings, our feet had already stepped onto the passageway that separates the men's and women's prison cells. After walking only a few steps here, I glimpsed four or five children outside the third fence gate ahead. It is said that those were four or five of the seven children trafficked from Guilin by two human traffickers who had been causing a stir in the neighborhood for several days, so we moved our steps towards the unlocked third fence gate. Outside this third fence gate, there is a desolate open space like a courtyard, and mosquitoes were singing beside the two or three puddles of sewage on the ground. Against the wall on the left is a small, dilapidated house with only the roof remaining. Inside the house, in front of a temporary stove made of three bricks on the ground, a woman in her thirties was stir-frying rice. According to the explanation of the female prison staff member standing next to her, this open space is the children's playground, and this temporary stove is where the female prisoners cook their own meals.

Coincidentally, the female prisoner had finished stir-frying the rice, and the female prison staff member wanted to send her back to the prison cell, so our group, large and small, all turned back inside the third fence gate, and walked about four or five feet to the right along the passageway, and arrived at the women's prison cell. Here, outside the door is also a row of very large wooden fences, and a five- or six-inch long padlock is placed across the fence gate. Between the wooden fence and the low bungalow that serves as the women's prison cell, there is still a piece of open space two or three feet wide. Seven or eight female prisoners were crowded in this open space, some standing, and two or three of them were making shoe soles, and one was knotting hemp. Inside the dark bungalow, there were more than ten female prisoners sitting there in a daze, each worrying about their own sorrows, and there were also two or three who were quietly making shoes. Among these twenty-odd female prisoners, except for the one standing by the prison cell door in a daze, who was only twenty-one or two years old, the rest, from the looks of it, were all over thirty, and some were probably approaching forty. Their expressions were mostly dull and sorrowful, and as for their complexion, it could be said to be uniform. Whether on their faces or arms, they would immediately remind one of a pair of bound feet that had been wrapped for decades, the kind of ashen white color when the foot binding cloths were just unwrapped.

The female prisoners seemed to be on very good terms with Ms. Suo Zhang. During the ten minutes we lingered outside their fence, several of them handed her the finished shoe soles to be taken to the customers outside. Because the general fee for someone to make shoes outside is one and a half dimes per shoe, and the rags and hemp thread are provided by the shoe owner, but when female prisoners make shoes for people, not only is the labor cost reduced to one dime, but the female prisoners must also provide their own hemp thread, so there are quite a few people who take the opportunity to take advantage of the situation and bring shoe soles for the female prisoners to make. In addition to asking her to bring shoe soles, there was another woman with a worried look on her face who earnestly asked Ms. Suo Zhang to help her write a petition. According to the female prison staff member, this woman is from a certain village in He County. Because of adultery with her uncle's son, she was sued by her husband and has now been sentenced to four months of imprisonment in Ping Le. However, her husband was not satisfied and is still asking the court to have her transferred to the detention center in her original hometown to imprison her, in order to shame her. The reason why she wants to write a petition is to state that she herself does not want to be transferred to another prison.

Leaving the prison cell, I talked with Ms. Suo Zhang for a while. She told me that among the male prisoners, there are cases of banditry, theft, land disputes, debt disputes, human trafficking, murder, etc., but among the female prisoners, nine out of ten are accused by their husbands or by their clansmen because of adultery. Even that youngest female prisoner standing by the door was also because she had another lover. One night, when her husband picked up a kitchen knife and ran to kill her lover, she had no choice but to help protect the person and killed her husband; she has now been sentenced to life imprisonment.

With my mind full of dark and terrible fantasies, I walked out of the detention center door. On the road, I thought of my cousin-in-law. Hasn't my cousin-in-law and the female perfumer in his store been having an affair for two years? My cousin knows all the details, and even helped them get abortions twice. Judging from the situation in the prison, if a married woman has an affair with someone, even if her own husband does not prosecute, the clansmen and people in society will still place her under the law; but if a married man -- like my cousin-in-law -- has an affair with someone, not only does his wife not sue him, but she also tries to take care of him, and the clansmen and people in society all say that he is very capable.

To put it another way, this unequal treatment of men and women in adultery cases has become a thing of the past. Now there are new regulations for absolutely equal criminal law for men and women; and according to the predictions of Mr. Wang Chonghui and Mr. Fu Bingchang, in the future, when this new criminal law is implemented, most husbands will be sued by their wives, and the prisons will be overcrowded due to the imprisonment of these married men. From now on, I will watch with new eyes, especially to see if my cousin will seize the magic weapon of the new provisions of Article 239 of the Criminal Law to sue her husband who has been having an affair for more than two years.

On George Sand 231

— Gou

If I wanted to find a great writer who has always been rebelling against reality in the past women's literature of various countries in the world, then I would think that only George Sand of France can be selected.

Most of the past women writers are nothing more than two types: the first is the appendage of nobles or official families, and the second is a prostitute-like figure who sells songs. The status given to women in history made it difficult for them to develop in other aspects except for being these two kinds of "talents." However, we do not deny that there are also one or two exceptions. The role of those one or two exceptions is often produced due to certain conditions during social changes, and their outstanding points are often even more surprising than those of accomplished men of the same era. This is a powerful factual counterattack against the theory that women are innately inferior to men advocated by those scientists who do not understand historicity. The great George Sand that I am going to talk about now is one of these outstanding roles.

Those who write literary history have always simply listed George Sand in romantic literature, and have summarily ignored her true value. For example, Lan Song, a relatively progressive literary historian in France, called her novels "lyrical novels" of romanticism when talking about her. But is George Sand really just a romantic lyrical novelist? I dare say no, absolutely not! We should correctly understand this great female writer, and we should rescue her from the fog.

George Sand was born into a noble family. She was the daughter of the landlord Du Pan, but she left her environment and went on a road that was completely opposite to her origin. She abandoned her husband, went to Paris alone, and used a rebellious pen to write a large number of works that opposed the social system at that time. At that time in France, it was the time when the July Revolution of 1848 was brewing, and this tide of social change pushed the kind people of the middle class with aristocratic blood flowing in their veins to a leaping future. George Sand appeared before us in this way.

Her early works such as "Lelia" and "Jacques" are called "love novels" by literary historians, but in fact, that is not the case at all. Those novels mainly focus on the issues of sex and marriage, and are definitely not simply about "love." George Sand believed that marriage must have love, that love can prevent marriage from becoming vulgar or tragic, and that marriage must have absolute freedom to be transformed into something sacred, that is, when the feelings between husband and wife break down, they must be free to divorce, and there should be no hypocrisy or accommodation. This theory may not seem new today, but at that time in Europe, it was the vanguard against the aristocratic marriage system. George Sand used the protagonists in her novels to prove all of this, and her attitude, like her own behavior, was extraordinarily firm and unambiguous.

However, the problems she delved into were not limited to this. After she expressed her opinions on the issues of sex and marriage in this way, she began to work on general social issues. Novels such as "The Miller of Angibautt" and "The Sin of Mr. Antoine" were her second step of work. In the former, the heroine is a female landlord who is willing to marry a worker; in the latter, the hero is an aristocrat who is willing to hand over his property after death to a landlord who is willing to sacrifice himself and implement a new system. She was almost relentlessly attacking the family property system, and she created many characters to speak on her behalf. We can say that her early works were her offerings to the human family problem, and her second step of social novels was the solution from human physiology to human economy. Needless to say, the society she idealized was not a truly realizable society, but that is another question, and she herself never failed to be great.

Her later works were completely inclined towards peasants, and the significance of this has not been explained in literary history. This is also not accidental. The society George Sand fundamentally idealized was one in which human beings could obtain physiological and economic freedom, and at the same time, she also recognized that to obtain this freedom, everything pressing on the people's heads must be denied. She was friends with Pierre Leroux and jointly published a publication that contributed to the revolution, and she had contact with many famous people in the labor movement at that time. She was pursuing her ideal, hoping that the revolution of 1848 would give her the realization of an ideal society. However, in fact, after the July Revolution, she did not get anything like what she had imagined. Not only did this make her very disappointed, but the result of this disappointment made her escape back to the countryside of her childhood. In these later works, such as "La Petite Fadtte" and "Francois le Champt", she described the deeds of peasants, but she never gave up her claims: she always directed her affirmative writing towards poor peasants and hardworking farmers, while she always used negative writing for landlords and others.

Everyone knows the love story between George Sand and the poet Musset, and everyone knows that George Sand later abandoned Musset, but no one has ever explained the social significance contained in this literary romance that has been passed down for thousands of years. In my opinion, the reason why George Sand could not finally live to old age with Musset was because their own thoughts were inconsistent. Musset was a representative of the declining aristocracy. He had welcomed Napoleon and even vilified the criminals who killed Louis Philippe. In his later work, "Confession d'nu enfant du Siecle", he would also criticize Voltaire. Such a reactionary poet would be very difficult to integrate with the populist George Sand. In this romance, we can precisely prove the irreconcilable differences between the two representatives of the aristocratic class after the split at that time.

In short, George Sand is a great writer, and I hope that literary historians, especially those who lavishly talk about women's literature, will use new perspectives to do some research on her. The purpose of this short article of mine is for this reason.

Current Status of American Laboring Women 232

— Li Xiuying

There are approximately 1,600,000 laboring women in the United States today. Proportionally by age, about 15% are under 20 years old, and 37% are under 25 years old. Among them, there are hundreds of thousands of child laborers.

They are mostly distributed in the textile industry, garment industry, food industry, leather industry, tobacco industry, and hardware industry.

Before Roosevelt's New Deal, their working hours were generally limited to no more than 54 hours per week (general wages in the United States are calculated on a weekly basis). However, these regulations were merely examples, and capitalists rarely complied. For instance, Pennsylvania law stipulates that women and child laborers should not work more than 54 hours per week. In reality, female workers had to work 11 or 12 hours a day.

After the New Deal was announced in the spring of 1933, only a small number of enterprises temporarily reduced working hours. For example, silk factories had weekly working hours of 36.9 hours in March 1933, which were reduced to 33.9 hours by September 1933. In the cotton weaving industry, weekly working hours in March 1933 were 44.1 hours, which were reduced to 35.8 hours by September of the same year. However, in other enterprises, the average weekly working hours in the fall of 1933 increased compared to March of the same year. For example, in tobacco factories, working hours increased from 36.5 hours to 38.5 hours per week; in the electrical machinery industry, they increased from 28 hours to 33.4 hours. Furthermore, capitalists forced workers to increase their labor rate and shorten their meal and bathroom break times during the reduced working hours to compensate for the losses incurred during the shortened time! For example, workers who previously manufactured 100 products in 60 hours per week now have to manufacture the same number of products in 40 hours.

Night work is still very common, although the laws of many states clearly prohibit female and child laborers from doing night work. However, capitalists do not comply. The example below is already a very "polite compliance" with the law: A female worker in New York State worked from 7:30 a.m. until 12:06 a.m. the next day, but her work record stated that she worked until 9:30 p.m. that day. When she argued with the foreman, the foreman said, "Yes, I know. But saying 9:30 p.m. sounds much better than saying 12:06 a.m.!"

American laboring women work such long hours, but their wages are pitifully low. Female workers who earn $14.30 for every 100 hours of work often say, "If I pay for food, I can't afford rent; if I pay rent, I have nothing to eat." However, these wages are higher compared to those of female workers in other enterprises—who are paid on a weekly basis. The wages of some female workers surveyed by a factory inspection team in 1933 were almost unbelievable, only one to five dollars per week!

From Roosevelt's New Deal, which stipulates that weekly wages should not be lower than $12 to $14, it seems that a daily wage of $2 is much higher than a weekly wage of $2. However, if one considers the current standard of living in the United States, it becomes clear that these "higher" wages still cannot sustain life. Moreover, in some places, the wages of female workers have actually decreased since the implementation of the New Deal. For example, in June 1933, the weekly wage of female workers in New York State was $12.53, a 16% decrease compared to the same month last year; the weekly wage of female workers in Illinois was $12.03 in December 1933, a 25% decrease compared to the same month last year. The decrease in wages is naturally related to the increase in unemployed workers in the United States during the economic panic—according to statistics from the Milton Institute, there were a total of 17,034,000 unemployed workers in the United States before May 1933. With so many unemployed workers, capitalists can pay workers very low wages.

Generally speaking, the wages of American laboring women are lower than those of men, with some differences reaching 50%. Moreover, the wages of Black female workers in the United States are even lower than those of White female workers. Black female workers are mostly distributed in manufacturing and machinery industries, tobacco factories, garment industries, food industries, and other enterprises. They mostly do those heavy, dirty, and "lowest-class jobs."

The wages earned by American laboring women are so meager, but the cost of living remains high. Especially since inflation, prices have uniformly increased. As a result, even employed female workers are in a state of semi-starvation. For example, a female worker with a typical weekly income of $4 has to spend $0.20 on transportation and $0.30 on food each day, totaling $0.50 per day, or $3 per week. With the remaining $1, she still has to pay for rent, electricity, clothes, etc. In addition to working long hours in factories, laboring women also have many tasks waiting for them at home: cooking, laundry, feeding children, etc.

Thus, excessive labor in factories every day, coupled with housework, severely depletes their vitality, causing them to age prematurely.

While thousands upon thousands of female workers are doing processing work, doing night work, ruining their health, and even losing their lives, on the other hand, there are nearly four million women who have lost their jobs and are waiting for work. Moreover, among all employed female workers, 27% are doing part-time work.

These facts prove that in the months following the implementation of Roosevelt's New Deal, the working hours of American female workers are still extended, wages are still meager, and the number of unemployed female workers continues to increase. At the same time, these facts also make American laboring women realize that relying on capitalists to seek happiness for workers is a dream. They can only rely on their own strength and strive hard to achieve everything they desire.

Overseas Women's News

— Shi

(1) Social Activities of Indian Women

Indian women, both in the past and present, have made significant contributions to science, religion, and the stability and happiness of society. However, organized activities have only recently begun.

Currently, their most important work is in the political sphere, namely participating in the Indian independence movement, fighting for freedom alongside men, and making enormous sacrifices. The women's suffrage movement began in 1917, when representatives of women across India visited Mr. Montagu, the British Secretary of State for India, who came to India, requesting equal political rights with men. Although the central parliament could not have female representatives, local governments granted them civil rights, giving millions of women the right to participate in politics within the scope of local politics. As a result, Dr. Reddi became the Deputy Speaker of the Madras Legislative Council.

In the British-Indian Round Table Conference in London, India had three female representatives in attendance. The recent constitution will grant six million women the right to participate in politics, with forty-four women serving as members of the state legislative assemblies.

The activities of Indian women are not limited to politics. They are also interested in education, social reform, social services, and other matters. Many women serve as lawyers, doctors, and professors.

The world-renowned educator Lady Lai is a member of the Calcutta University Council. In 1927, two female judges were appointed in the major cities of Bombay and Madras. Bombay has about sixteen female judges, and Madras has even more.

In 1920, India not only granted women the right to participate in politics but also appointed two women as legislative members. A female member of the Travancore legislature became the Minister of Health, and the famous female poet Naidu was elected as the Speaker of the Indian National Congress during the parliamentary session in 1925.

The Indian representative who began attending the Geneva League of Nations Commission this year to discuss issues related to the trafficking of women and children is also a woman.

Indian women, realizing the mission they bear in life, strive to develop the women's movement despite their weak abilities and regardless of obstacles ahead, hoping to contribute to humanity.

(2) Spanish Government Appoints Women as Special Ambassadors

Ms. Espina, a famous Spanish female writer, was recently appointed by the government as a special ambassador to attend the national founding ceremony of Peru in South America in 1935. It is also rumored that Ms. Espina will be the recipient of the next Nobel Prize.

(3) Nicaragua Appoints Female Diplomats

The President of Nicaragua in Central America, Sacasa, appointed two female diplomats two months ago, one being Ms. Argilu, the Vice Consul of Virginia, USA, and the other being Ms. Lomeru, the Consul of San Diego, California.

(4) Statistics on Current Working Women in Japan

Commercial employees - 998,261

Transportation industry - 997,251

Factory laborers - 3,075,000

Domestic servants - 572,864

In addition to rural women engaged in agriculture, working women in Japan account for 3.6/10 of the total population.

Remuneration Regulations

The time for this office to issue compensation is from the 6th to the 10th and from the 16th to the 20th of each month. Except for Sundays, the Accounting Office of this office will issue payments from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM daily. Please prepare a voucher, affix a stamp identical to the original manuscript, and directly collect the payment. If collecting multiple months together, vouchers must still be prepared and stamped separately for each month for easy attachment to the ledger. Regarding the stamping, regardless of the length of the article or the number of submissions per month, please stamp each article to facilitate verification of the seal when collecting the compensation. Articles without stamps will be treated as renouncing compensation. Furthermore, the compensation period expires six months from the date of publication. If it remains unclaimed by the deadline, it will be considered unwillingness to receive compensation, and the account will be closed to finalize the matter.

Please promptly send the stamps to facilitate the collection of remuneration.

Commercial News

Revival of Popularity in Financial and Gold Markets Is Difficult 233

Banks Pounce on Foreign Exchange, Once Breaking 90 Yuan

Balance Tax Was Low, Eventually Falling 1.1 Yuan

Yesterday, the gold market saw a consistent drop in British and American silver prices. It immediately rose upon opening, but optimism was still difficult to maintain. Banks lacked a selling appetite and instead pounced on settlement, causing the domestic market to tighten suddenly, briefly breaking through the 90-yuan mark. Subsequently, the balance tax was lowered by 0.025, the foreign exchange market stabilized, and confidence ultimately waned. As a result, continued declines were seen. The deteriorated confidence truly disheartened buyers. Upon inspection, overseas silver markets saw consistent declines in British and American markets, with the forward silver price in Montevideo also falling by half a point. Exchange rates uniformly decreased, and London spot gold fell by 3.5 pence. Over-the-counter pre-market trading opened at 88.9 yuan, showing no firm rise, leading to a setback immediately after opening. When the Central Bank announced its benchmark prices, the British remained stable while the American shrank by 0.0125, the customs gold unit fell by 0.0005, and the standard gold price retreated to 1010.2 yuan before continuing to decline. However, the opening was still high, and the market remained relatively stable after opening. Banks showed no selling appetite and instead pounced on settlement, leading to a situation where demand exceeded supply and gradually pushed the price upward. Although there was intraday consolidation, the domestic market remained tight, and banks' buying appetite was exceptionally strong. Sen Changyong persistently purchased, causing the gold price to break through the 90-yuan mark. However, due to the continued selling by large accounts, the market stabilized slightly thereafter. The announcement of the silver balance tax, lowered by 0.00025 and levied at 6.75%, calculated with the British exchange rate at 1 shilling 5.6875 pence, made further rises difficult. Hua Shang's sentiment weakened, and the foreign exchange market also turned stable. The gold market gradually declined. Subsequently, Western banks even started unloading, and the foreign exchange market slightly loosened. Confidence was already poor, and the selling momentum was triggered, making it difficult to control. Buyers' intentions turned pessimistic, leading to a decline. However, because the foreign exchange market remained stable, it was difficult to settle American dollars at 33.375 yuan for February. After the price decreased, there was still support, and the market rebounded around noon. Upon inspecting the morning market conditions, it was initially firm but then weakened, resulting in a continued decline. Looking ahead, it is feared that a rising trend will be difficult to form before the swap period because buyers, restricted by unfavorable swaps, will not dare to act rashly. Now, the morning market conditions are recorded as follows:

The opening was 987.1 yuan, 1 yuan higher than the previous close. Fuxing Yongyuan sold positions, reducing the price to 6.4 yuan. Citibank purchased spot shillings at 5.6875 pence. Dadecheng and Fuchang bought in limited quantities, and the situation remained stable. MacKay purchased U.S. dollars for January at 75. Hengyu, Tongchun, Hengxing, Hongxing, Yuanyi, Yuanchang, Yongfu, Xingzhaofeng, and Changlian all bought together, raising the price to 8.7 yuan. Jinfeng, Yongyongfeng, Dayuan, Fuxing, Yongqing, Yushunmao sold positions, reducing the price to 7.5 yuan. However, the domestic market was extremely tight. Jiaotong purchased shillings for January at 375. Sentiment was positive. Qianchangxiang and Dachangxiang settled with Hengyu, stabilizing the market. Subsequently, Zhejiang purchased U.S. dollars for January at 6875. Sen Changyong, Yuanchangyong, Yuli, Hengchangyong, and Dadecheng continued to purchase. Yuqingyong sold, but because the bank wanted to settle U.S. dollars for January at 625, the price once rose to 91 yuan. Securities and Public Bonds Fluctuate, Momentum Shaken 237

Yesterday, the Chinese Securities Exchange and foreign exchange rates remained unchanged. As the Fifth Plenary Session is approaching, logically, there should be a slight increase. However, there was an overabundance of bulls, mostly speculative and insubstantial. Political rumors suddenly emerged in the market, including talk of issuing 24th Year public bonds, causing the bull momentum to falter. Market prices then trended downwards. At this time of high bull positions, even slight rumors easily cause declines but make rises difficult. As the reporter previously mentioned, unfortunately, this prediction came true. Current market conditions still show excessively high forward prices, with foreign exchange rates exceeding one percent interest, making arbitrage unprofitable. Therefore, there are few buyers for forward contracts. When buying, it is more profitable to focus on recent contracts. However, market speculators are buying distant contracts instead of recent ones. This is a weakness of the bulls. If foreign exchange rates do not ease and arbitrage does not stimulate activity, market prices will not easily rise. With the opening of the conference, even slight rumors are enough to shake the market. Therefore, there are still waves ahead. Yesterday's activity showed initial firmness at the opening, with news of troop reduction and "19 Customs" bonds. However, supply gradually exceeded demand, and the "50 Bond" saw some selling, leading to a slight decrease of one or two jiao. As the trend changed, market sentiment shifted. As a result, the secondary market saw a unanimous downward trend, with the "50 Bond" and others continuing to be sold, falling another one or two jiao, leading to the rise of rumors. In the afternoon, sentiment was weak, rumors persisted, and prices fell another three or four jiao. The market failed to stabilize at the close, continuing to fall two or three jiao. Bullish selling slightly increased. In the end, market prices fell from one or two jiao to seven or eight jiao. The outlook is not optimistic. The total trading volume was 9,635,000 yuan.
