US Cotton Utilization

New York, December 7th Telegram Reports on the Cotton Market Situation for the Week: At the beginning of this week, bull liquidations and Southern sales were absorbed by the market. Prices strengthened after President Roosevelt announced his attitude towards the Bankhead Act. It is believed that President Roosevelt's proposal to exempt farmers producing no more than two bales of cotton from restrictions will secure President Roosevelt's endorsement of the proposal at the Farmers' Referendum Assembly on December 14th. After the market price rose, retail investors liquidated and Southern sellers also sold slightly. However, traders wanted to wait for the government cotton production report or other driving forces. Agricultural Adjustment Administration (AAA) personnel estimated that cotton production under the voluntary cotton field consolidation program, if the Bankhead Act continues to be implemented, would be around 12 million bales. If it does not continue, cotton production may be around 13 million bales. Some parties purchased October futures during the week because the new cotton price discount would be reduced if the Bankhead Act continued. However, traders believe that the tight spot cotton market will keep old cotton prices high. At the same time, traders are more concerned about the distribution of cotton than the possible changes in cotton supply figures.

Grain Futures – Flour and Wheat Markets Recover 243

Flour: After the opening of the market yesterday morning, the prices of all months showed a stable fluctuation. As for the quotation of foreign wheat, there was a difference of 48 points between Chicago. Outside of Canada, it was 8 points to 10 jiao. When the price was opened, due to the continuation of the previous day's foreign wheat, the sentiment of the outsiders was quite loose. Then, the enthusiasm of various factories to sell near and even all periods was reduced. Although the issue of tax increases has come to an end for the time being, it is not yet certain whether it can be fulfilled according to the manufacturers' requests in the future. The lack of strong factory selling and the stabilization of sentiment are undoubtedly related. By the time the afternoon market opened, sentiment in both near and distant months had gradually rebounded. Since the outsiders were floating short, they were deeply afraid that foreign wheat would change again due to Saturday and that the fluctuations would be huge. Therefore, a small number of floating shorts gradually covered their positions. In addition, the buying interest of outsiders did not decrease, and the shouting price gradually increased. As a result, this month's price rebounded by 1 fen and 2.5 li compared to the previous day, January's price rebounded by 1 fen and 2.5 li, February's price rebounded by 1.5 fen, March's price rebounded by 2 fen, April's price rebounded by 1.5 fen, and May's price rebounded by 1 fen and 2.5 li.

Wheat: Yesterday's wheat futures market showed a stable trend in all months after the morning opening. The quotation for foreign wheat had little fluctuation. When the price was opened, due to the fact that the buying and selling of insiders and outsiders had not decreased for a long time, the transaction was lonely and there was no change. By the time the afternoon market opened, the flour market was tired but firm, and the increase in tax on foreign wheat was not yet certain, so the buying interest in near and distant months was relatively strong, and the price was raised by 2-3 fen. According to the bottom price of domestic wheat, there is still an opportunity for improvement in the later stages. As a result, this month's price was better by 3 fen, and February's price was better by 3 fen. There were no other changes. The spot wheat market saw good performance in high-quality wheat, up 12 fen, while the middle and lower grades were flat. Shandong Guide wheat opened at 4 yuan, Xuzhou Bengbu wheat opened at 3 yuan 9 jiao 89 fen, and Yaowan wheat opened at 3 yuan 9 jiao 56 fen. 12,000 bags were taken by Fuxin and 2,000 bags were taken by Shenda.

Chicago wheat benefited from the delay in transportation and sales, not from the lack of domestic supply. However, because it has approached the import base price, the strong wheat price may only be a flash in the pan. The winter wheat situation is very good. News from Winnipeg indicates that Canada may sell 50 million bushels of frozen wheat to the United States, causing prices to fall back.

River Rice Stagnant, Suddenly Softens 244

(South Shanghai) The sources of various goods are still only about 30 firms (a total of nearly 5,000 piculs). Sales are weakening, and the market color is declining. Although various late-season rice continued to be purchased by Qingdao firms for more than 400 bags, they fell by an angle of one angle. Early rice from Nan Gang is stagnant and has fallen by an angle, with the exception of the Su Tong gang japonica, which is relatively rare and can barely stand firm. Du Yangjian's arrival at the port is rare, and sentiment is slightly stabilized. Those in the middle market can barely stand firm, while those with high prices have shown signs of weakness. The change in yuan means that the road is turning stagnant and has suddenly fallen by 1-2 jiao.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 16-17 ships arrived from various roads under the river. In terms of market sales, white japonica demand is sparse, and demand for sheep Du Jianzao rice is normal. Bai Yuan Yinyuan are settled separately, and demand from liquor dealers is flat. The price of Bai Jing Yang Du Jianzao rice is stable, and the price of Bai Yuan Yinyuan is slightly tighter.

Foreign Rice – One Ship Delayed Due to Wind Resistance 245

Spot Foreign Rice Rises by an Angle

Yesterday, the foreign rice market was very good because local customers' demand continued to be strong. Yesterday, Yongbang also made a small jiao futures of 2,000 tons and spot foreign rice of 3,000 bags, making the market more lively. In addition, the company ship Erli Caipeisimala, which was loaded with Saigon rice, encountered wind and waves in Nanyang and berthed in Singapore for repairs, so it needs to be postponed for two weeks before arriving in Shanghai. After this news spread, the atmosphere in the market was very tense. Saigon Siamese rice transactions were very strong, opening as many as 13,800 bags, and the price also rose by an angle. In addition to Yongbang's small jiao purchase in futures (Dafu sold it, February 4 yuan 8 jiao, price rose 5 fen), 200 tons were also recycled. Ke Xian opened a total of 6,700 bags and was distributed by local streets in the mainland. Because the origin reported a rise, the owners of the goods mainly shouted high, so the selling price was greatly closer to an angle to 2 jiao.

Soybean Trading Volume is Not Weak 246

Yesterday, the soybean market, regardless of the soybeans on the Jinpu and Longhai lines, rose by 2-3 fen to 6-7 fen. The reason is that the rumored large-scale sources have not yet arrived, and the arrival is likely to be small. The Shanghai inventory is not thick, and the local road is tight, so the market situation has risen. Yesterday, the Guide bean market opened at 3 yuan, 5 jiao, 3 fen, up 3 fen compared to the previous market. Xinanzhen big grain beans opened at 3 yuan, 5 jiao, 6 fen. Hankou Zhaza beans opened for more than 3,000 bags, with prices ranging from 3 yuan 3 jiao 2 fen to 3 yuan 2 jiao. The high bean market continued to rise by 2 fen, and the middle and lower goods had to be raised by 6-7 fen. There are also Hankou Che Dou Chi Dou Gou Dou, the market also continued to rise by 2-3 fen. Jiujiang beans are also tight. Dalian Siping Daidou still opened at 4 yuan, the big grain seed rose by 2 fen, and the price was 4 yuan 3 jiao. Yesterday, a total of more than 6,700 bags of various beans were traded in the general market.

Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Confession of a Female Clerk

Bread for Bread's Sake 270

— By Shen Lisu

Female Staff Member of the Bread Department at the China National Products Company

Interview with Miss Hua Yingying

Last winter, I finished my last lesson at the "Yan Mou Shi" Girls' School, completing a phase of my academic journey. During the solemn and enthusiastic graduation ceremony, I received a diploma amid the kind and smiling face of the principal.

Although many commercialized universities with their "open the school gates wide, no money, no entry" policy are waiting and welcoming the children of the wealthy, I am not a noble's daughter. Therefore, I had to abandon that rosy dream.

At the same time, I wondered whether I could truly satisfy my thirst for knowledge at a university. Moreover, even if there were profound academic principles worth learning, would they meet the needs of future society? These questions were somewhat related to my decision not to keep taking university entrance exams.

Distrusting modern university education, I decided to end my life as a student and become a laborer engaged in practical social work. When I shared this idea with my family, the elders unsympathetically rejected it. Their reasons were similar to those generally used to suppress women's employment, believing that women's professions were merely nominal and that women lacked the ability to work. They even said that even if society allowed women's professions to develop freely, its purpose was merely to use women to attract more of the desired clientele.

The elders in my family thought this way, and most people in society could not escape this paradigm. They were like black clouds obstructing the bright future of women's professions.

Later, the elders could not resist my firm conviction and allowed me to become a member of the intellectual workforce.

I started working here in the spring of this year, so it has been less than a year. Based on my experience during this time, I believe the future development of women's professions will not be discouraged by current social obstacles.

The company treats female and male employees equally and does not discriminate. However, due to physiological differences, female employees' work capabilities are often not as brave and lively as those of male employees. This is my subjective feeling, but based on the actual situations I have seen with female employees at work, there probably isn't a big difference.

When I first joined, my monthly salary was only eighteen yuan, but after two months, it was raised to twenty-four yuan. As of recently, my labor is worth thirty yuan a month.

Is this a lot of income? Of course! Human desires are endless, and one will not be satisfied with thirty yuan a month. Is it little? But looking closely at the current economic situation in society, even if I have a belly full of aspirations, I can't help but feel discouraged.

Speaking honestly, I am quite satisfied with my labor compensation. However, the work is too mechanical, and I can't help but feel a bit unhappy, like a snake coiling in my heart. Perhaps this is what is called "doing one job, complaining about it," a manifestation of the desire for novelty and aversion to the old. Generally, every professional inevitably has a sense of timidity. Most young people working in an organized and disciplined group prefer activity to stillness. Although this is a commercial group, its systematic management and strict discipline are not inferior to those of other group organizations. The department to which a certain item belongs and the specific duties of each employee are clearly and strictly defined.

The department I work in is the "Bread Department," which is part of the "Food Department." Across from the "Bread Department" is the "Candy Department," and each department has a female employee. The one in the "Candy Department" is my younger sister – Yingying.

The work in the "Bread Department" and "Candy Department" involves more stillness than activity. Although it can be busy at times, the work is too easy and I don't feel excited or interested. However, selling bread and candy, although simple, sometimes requires careful handling!

When a customer comes to buy bread, you need to know how to pick it up so that it doesn't lose its original beautiful packaging;

Page 21

This work seems extremely simple and easy, but if you are slightly careless, it can lose its original smoothness because your hand gripped it too tightly. Customers spend money to buy bread, so they can freely choose. If you hand them one that looks ugly, they will refuse the first one you offer. If the one you offer next is the same, they will leave disappointed. Although we – either the employees or the customers – all know that the appearance of the bread has nothing to do with its taste, most customers still pay attention to its external appearance.

The working hours here are from 9:00 a.m. to 8:00 p.m., a full eleven hours. It's not long, but it's not short either. Compared to the usual working hours in Chinese stores, ours are quite moderate. Although I sometimes feel mentally exhausted due to the long working hours, in the current era where the American eight-hour system has not been implemented, it cannot be said that the capitalists' treatment is harsh.

Chinese stores still operate during meal times, which is a common phenomenon, so of course, we are no exception. There is half an hour to leave the job during meal times. The employees of each department are divided into several shifts and take turns going to the "canteen" to eat. Someone remains on duty at the counter to make sales.

Lunch is from 12:00 to 1:30 p.m., and dinner is from 6:00 to 7:30 p.m. During this time, meals are served continuously, as lively as a "flowing water" banquet in a restaurant. The company provides all the meals, so employees don't have to spend extra money. Also, the company takes care of the accommodation for a small number of male employees and trainees.

To be fair, as far as I know, several companies of roughly the same size treat their male and female employees somewhat worse. The starting salary here is eighteen yuan, and it increases quickly, sometimes by two yuan or four yuan, and at most by six yuan, depending on the work performance. Other companies probably don't have such figures, and most of their salary increases have a rigid rule, with some increasing only after a year and others increasing twice a year. This kind of salary increase method conceals a harmful flaw for the company, which the company authorities cannot easily detect. Let me give a simple example to illustrate this flaw: For example, if an employee knows that the company's salary increase is held once a year, he can be lazy at ordinary times, perfunctorily doing his job carelessly. But when the salary increase is approaching, he can be as excited as a machine with extra oil, doing his job vigorously. Between his diligence and laziness, the company suffers a huge loss invisibly, but his salary still increases the same as other employees. This situation is like a student who usually doesn't study hard and only "burns the midnight oil" to intensify his work during the big exam. Although he manages to pass the exam, the knowledge still jumps out of his stomach in his haste. A school doesn't suffer losses from having this kind of student, but a company faces a great danger from having this kind of employee!

The company authorities seem to have also sensed this customer psychology. Therefore, although the bread sold here may not entirely suit the tastes of noble sons and daughters, they are unwilling to display items made from substandard materials.

There are probably more than a dozen types of bread sold here, as well as dozens of expensive cakes. The prices range from five cents to several dimes per piece. Beautiful decorations and neat packaging often make general customers willing to pay a high price to possess something with a beautiful appearance whose actual taste they don't even know. Therefore, among the dozens of types of bread and cakes, the decoration of a single piece of bread can cost several cents. On the consumer side, I often feel that society is becoming more and more decadent. Fortunately, the consumables I see are produced by domestic factories, which gives me a lot of peace of mind.

Although I have spent almost a year here, I still feel that there are many things worth learning carefully. For example, when I encounter a customer who isn't afraid of trouble, I am afraid of the trouble first. At the time, I felt that this thought was reasonable, but when I think back on it, I can't help but feel a little ashamed. Because when a customer comes to buy something, they instinctively choose the quality of the goods and the level of prices. Although some customers' attitudes toward choosing goods are not sincere, they always have the right to choose. The duty of a salesperson is to display as many similar goods as possible for them to choose from. There is absolutely no reason to refuse them the right to choose. Even if you encounter an irrational customer whose intentions are "not about the wine but about the scenery," the salesperson can try to understand them, then think of ways to deal with them separately, and absolutely not give them any bad blows because of the customer's frivolous attitude. Because losing a customer is a great loss for the company, but at the same time, it invisibly affects the future of the entire women's profession, and this loss is difficult to estimate. In this unreasonable society, the future of women's professions is covered with thorns. If we don't have the courage to cut through the thorns, then it's better to go back to the family and prepare to be someone's virtuous wife and good mother!

When I first started working in the bread department, I encountered many customers who came to buy bread with malicious intent. At that time, I really wanted to quit. But in the end, reason overcame the environment, and those unkind customers seemed to feel tired and gradually disappeared. Now, they can be said to have disappeared completely.

The company also takes the attitude of employees towards customers very seriously and absolutely does not allow employees to be impolite. There is now a training class for trainees to train them in basic business knowledge and applied English. During the day, trainees practice greeting customers politely and sales techniques in the marketplace, while also delivering invoices and collecting money in various departments.

I've already said a lot and should stop. But I can't bear to give up this opportunity to talk, so I might as well say it frankly!

Recently, I have often received letters from many unknown people who are very concerned about my private life. Some even advise me not to go to dance halls and not to engage in meaningless social interactions, which really makes me feel ashamed and grateful! Heavens! Are these people who write to me really well-intentioned? In this crime-filled social environment, I really dare not believe it, because even my parents are not always this concerned about me. However, here I cannot help but be grateful for their kindness and express myself.

To be frank, eleven hours of work every day is enough to exhaust all my energy. When I come back from the company, my legs often don't obey me. If I were to go to a dance hall to enjoy that kind of revelry, only I know that I don't have that courage!

I don't absolutely deny leisure entertainment. However, when I am occasionally mentally excited, I will quietly go to the cinema to watch a movie or be with my sister. In fact, reading novels is also a form of entertainment, so sometimes novels are my entertainment object. Also, playing ping-pong is something that my sister -- Yingying -- and I often do.

These people who write to me and care about my private life, it's not necessary to investigate whether their motives are well-intentioned, but at least they always haven't clearly understood the living environment of a professional.

Speeches

Starting from the Oversupply of Intellectuals 271

— By Liu Xin

In a world of economic recession, the "unemployment problem" has stumped most politicians and economists. Naturally, the oversupply of intellectuals makes the path for intellectuals even more difficult.

The Chinese have always held a "careerism" view of reading. Abolishing the imperial examination created a new kind of imperial examination: graduating from primary school is like passing the county-level exam, graduating from middle school is like passing the provincial-level exam, and a university diploma is naturally the ticket to the top scholar position. The traditional result of "study to become an official" is that most people tend towards liberal arts, and the path for most intellectuals is already designated as politics. However, the door to politics is too narrow, so liberal arts university students can only fall into the path of oversupply and unemployment. As for university students who study practical subjects, they also face the same path of confusion and unemployment, either because national industries are not yet developed, or because they lack real skills.

The Union of Vocational Movements of University Graduates already reflects all these phenomena.

Since intellectuals cannot enter the door to politics, they lower their standards and flock to the education sector to make a living. Graduates from education, liberal arts, law, and other departments all take the education sector as their final destination and as a place to wait for vacancies. Because Chinese education is not yet developed, the ratio of the number of middle schools to the number of primary school graduates each year is still far apart. The government does not yet have the financial resources to increase the number of schools, so private schools are springing up like mushrooms after the rain to accommodate this group of surplus university students. This kind of school is especially common in Shanghai.

Let us further examine the content of these schools: In terms of equipment, they are naturally simple and crude. If they can fill the bookshelves with textbooks to form a library, and slightly equip a few instruments and glass bottles to form a laboratory, then this school is considered top-notch. In terms of curriculum, one reason is that teachers' salaries are low, so it is naturally difficult to have excellent teachers to fill the positions. Also, for the sake of the school's finances, most subjects are simple and incomplete. It is even commonplace for teachers to be absent from class.

The most exhausting thing for those who run private schools is the problem of enrollment. The economic life of private schools depends entirely on students. In Shanghai alone, there are many private schools, and the source of students is limited, so they have to cast a wide net, using advertising to supplement the deficiencies, and using the weaknesses of students or parents to do everything possible to attract and lure them. This is a fact: It is said that the advertising fees spent by various private schools on enrollment in the newspapers during the summer vacation are no less than five or six hundred yuan. Alas - a magnificent institution of learning is transformed into a marketplace for merchants to solicit customers. If you say that Chinese education is not failing with this kind of education, there is no justice!

Of course, since the relationship between schools and students is built on a monetary relationship, and is not rooted in academic research, it is inevitable that it is difficult to implement strict systems in school management and teaching. As soon as you walk into a school, you can smell the atmosphere of arrogance and disorder. I once heard someone say: "Strictness doesn't work! If you are strict, the students will run away. Where will we get the money to pay for the eight or nine hundred yuan monthly rent and the food for dozens of people?" This is truly a "penetrating criticism"!

The countryside is bankrupt. Natural disasters and man-made disasters have brought the middle and lower classes in the countryside closer to the poverty line. When large stores and large companies are frantically shouting about big discounts, big sales, and big sacrifices, our schools are also very depressed because the purchasing power of students or parents is weak. Our intellectuals - the leaders of the schools - seeing that their careers are about to fail miserably, cannot help but make a final struggle and propose a method of reducing tuition fees, which is the same meaning as the "special" big sales and "desperate" big discounts of large companies and large stores. Poor students who come to study still cannot increase as expected.

The problem is gradually expanding. How do we get money for rent, meals, salaries, ...? - Teachers demand wages, principals run away, and then schools close ... Scenes emerge endlessly in the education sector.

This is not just a simple education problem, but has actually intricately formed a social problem. If we do not rectify the source from a political perspective and place the economic structure on a stable cornerstone, then this phenomenon may just be in full swing!

Casual Chat

In Memory of Mr. Shi Liangcai 272

— By Xu Zhi

Mr. Shi Liangcai was shot and killed by thugs on the afternoon of the 13th of last month on his way from Hangzhou to Shanghai. This shocking and unfortunate news has already spread throughout China and abroad, shaking the hearts of the general public. Although nearly a month has passed, there is still no news of the case being solved. At the same time, people from all walks of life in Shanghai, deeply saddened by Mr. Shi's tragic misfortune, will hold a grand memorial service for Mr. Shi to express their condolences. In this situation, I really don't know what words to use to express the grief and indignation in my heart regarding Mr. Shi's misfortune!

Mr. Shi was the general manager of this newspaper. He took over the "Shen Bao" after the founding of the Republic of China. The fact that the "Shen Bao's" business has been able to develop more and more and is in its current state can be said to be entirely the result of Mr. Shi's unique talent and hard work in planning. Now, the "Shen Bao" sells more than 100,000 copies every day, and its various supplements are also loved by a wide range of readers. At the same time, the various subsidiary businesses established under the "Shen Bao" Newspaper, such as the amateur tutoring school, the circulating library, the yearbook, the monthly magazine, etc., have made undeniable contributions to Chinese culture and Chinese society. Although it cannot be said that all these undertakings are entirely the achievement of Mr. Shi Liangcai alone, there is no doubt that Mr. Shi was the main driving force for realizing them. Now, the various cultural undertakings of the "Shen Bao" Newspaper are developing, but Mr. Shi Liangcai, the main driving force for these undertakings, has unfortunately passed away. This is not only a loss for the "Shen Bao" Newspaper, but also a major loss for the Chinese cultural world!

At the same time, Mr. Shi Liangcai not only worked hard in cultural undertakings, but also actively promoted general social undertakings. For example, he and Mr. Huang Yizhu founded the "Zhongnan Bank," he and Mr. Xiang Songmao founded the "Wuzhou Pharmacy," he and Mr. Lu Feibohong founded the "Zhonghua Book Company," and he founded the "Minsheng Yarn Factory," etc., all of which have brought great benefits to Chinese society. During the "January 28th Incident," the entire Shanghai was in a very dangerous state of turmoil, and most compatriots were panicking all day long, not knowing what to do. At this time, Mr. Shi came forward to initiate the establishment of the "Shanghai Local Maintenance Association" to deal with everything. Therefore, when it was changed to the "Local Coordination Association," Mr. Shi was still appointed as the chairman. In addition, Mr. Shi held many positions, such as the Speaker of the Municipal Council, the Director of the China Merchants Group, the Honorary Chairman of the Red Cross Society, and the Director of the Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center. These are all very important positions that have a great relationship with Chinese society. Therefore, Mr. Shi's misfortune is not only a loss for the Chinese cultural world, but also a huge loss for the entire Chinese society! Not only people in the Chinese cultural world feel deep sadness about this, but the general public also feels very grief-stricken!

Now, the date of the Shanghai people's memorial service for Mr. Shi is approaching. In this time of universal mourning and heart-wrenching sights, in addition to hoping that the government will solve this case as soon as possible, and hoping that the people of society and the working masses will continue Mr. Shi's spirit and work hard in cultural and general social work, the editor has written this article to commemorate Mr. Shi, not only to express mourning.

Page 22

Not having a clear understanding is always a fact. I am not complaining about people writing to me, but at least the people who write should carefully consider what meaning there is in writing this kind of letter.

Alright, I have said everything about my public and private life here. In the future, people who care about me can save some postage stamps and the energy they spend, and transfer it to the development of their own careers!

Common Knowledge

A Method of Selling 273

— Le Sheng

Selling is an art. Some salespeople can use methods that make buyers willingly purchase goods. Others not only fail to attract customers but also drive away those interested in the goods because of their ignorance of selling techniques. This difference is naturally due to the salesperson's skill.

There are, of course, many selling techniques, which can be utilized according to each individual's intelligence. However, there is one extremely fundamental and common selling technique that I want to discuss here, which all salespeople must be familiar with and pay great attention to. This is a selling technique based on the psychological principle of "Repetition." The "Repetition" principle is as follows: "Appropriate repetition of a certain phenomenon can arouse greater interest and attention in people." For example, if there are five advertisements, their effectiveness when posted in five different locations is often less than when posted in one location because a single poster often fails to arouse people's interest and attention. We often see that "posters" for Peking opera houses and movie theaters on the street are always pasted together in multiple copies; this is the same principle. There are many such examples in personal matters as well. We often have the experience that when we want to go to a certain place two or three miles away, we don't have a definite idea about whether to take a rickshaw or not. If at this time, many rickshaw pullers suddenly come one after another to solicit business, we might end up taking one of the later ones. "Life's major events" can often achieve satisfactory results due to continuous "pursuit" over and over again. The principle of selling is the same. When a customer arrives, needless to say, you must pleasantly take out the goods and ask them to inspect them. You must not be afraid of trouble, offering your goods to them once, twice, three times, four times... Only attentive service can persuade the buyer and win their favor. You must be like a rickshaw puller grabbing business or a young man pursuing a partner, persevering and not missing your opportunity to advance. Even a customer who is not very interested in the goods may be conquered by your attentiveness, and they will definitely choose an item to buy. (The last item presented often has a higher chance of being chosen.)

Many people have succeeded in selling by applying this "repetition" principle of once, twice, and thrice. In our country, salespeople in North China understand this principle better than those in Central and South China. In North China, more reputable shops, such as fabric stores, silver shops, and jewelry stores, will invite you to sit in a specially set-up reception room inside once you enter. Tea and cigarettes are offered, and the goods you want are brought one by one. Even if you are not satisfied, they will not blame you and will still politely send you out. Most smaller shops are also very polite and would never behave like the salespeople in some large shops in Shanghai, who show displeasure and impatience to customers who are not very interested in the goods, even scolding "pigs" or other insulting words. In fact, being polite to customers is absolutely necessary. You must know that offending one customer means losing one customer. How can people who rely on customers for food do something that is detrimental to themselves?

The Japanese are generally good at business and understand the tricks even better than the Chinese in the North. Their application of the "repetition" principle can be seen from their relentless approach to customers. No wonder Japanese merchants can be found in every corner of the world and succeed everywhere they go.

Amateur Cafe

Criticism, Abuse, and Beautiful Writing 274

A fair critic "neither cries nor laughs" at the person or work he criticizes; he merely explains its correctness or errors and the reasons for them. Naturally, in his explanation, he may sometimes express respect or "rebuke" for the person or work he criticizes, but if his position is correct and his reasons are just and sufficient, then the resulting "respect" or "rebuke" is not "boosting" or "abuse," but objective truth.

However, abuse is never criticism; criticism is rational, while abuse is unreasonable! Recently, some people who write "critical articles" do not understand this principle. They don't want theory, they just scold others as "absurd" or "idiotic" without pointing out where their "absurdity" or "idiocy" lies; sometimes they even completely deviate from the issue being discussed and focus on making a big "deal" out of the person's surname or given name. Such "criticism" cannot be considered criticism; it is merely unreasonable abuse. If the study and debate of all academics and all issues must have theoretical content in order to advance research and debate and to bring us closer to the truth, then those gentlemen who replace criticism with abuse are objectively hindering the progress of research and debate and are therefore obscuring the truth.

Those gentlemen who replace criticism with abuse say that some people cannot be reasoned with. Reasoning with such people is actually like playing the lute to a cow, so you can only give them a good scolding--such an argument seems very heroic on the surface, but fundamentally, it is an expression of incompetence in deliberately avoiding the issue. Because critical writing is not only for the person being criticized but also mainly for the general readers. It not only needs to be shown to the person being criticized but also to the general readers. But what can make the person being criticized speechless and at a loss for words is correct theory, not "a good scolding." What general readers are exploring is even more correct theory, not some "art of scolding." So if anyone wants to replace criticism with abuse, no matter what their "reason" is, it is an expression of incompetence in failing to meet legitimate objective demands.

If this phenomenon of replacing criticism with abuse continues to develop, then not only will all research and debate be hindered, but criticism itself may be in danger of being eliminated. Think about it: if everyone thinks that it is right to replace criticism with abuse, and all those who write critical articles use various excuses to desperately show off their "talent" by blindly scolding the people they criticize, then will there still be criticism? Therefore, for the sake of the very life of criticism, we cannot agree with any reason for replacing criticism with abuse. We need to reveal the truth, and we demand theoretical criticism and debate!

Just as it is wrong to replace criticism with abuse, it is also wrong to only want to write a "beautiful article" with beautiful words and an unusual structure, regardless of whether the critical writing is theoretically correct or not. We know that words and writing are used to express our thoughts and feelings. There must first be a certain thought and feeling, and then there are words and writing suitable for expressing this thought and feeling; even aestheticism, which specializes in words and phrases, and Chinese parallel prose, which specializes in the splendor and antithesis of words, are produced under certain thoughts and feelings. Theory is a systematic combination of thoughts and feelings. Therefore, we must focus on theory when writing critical articles, with words being secondary--words are tools for expressing theory--and we cannot focus solely on the beauty of words, lest we fall into the pit of "harming the meaning with words." For example, when we want to criticize someone's theory, we must have our own theoretical system, and then find words suitable for expressing our opinions within this theoretical system to write a theoretical critical article. In the middle of this, even if there are many beautiful words, witty scolding, and profound classical references, if they are not suitable for expressing our theory, then they should be discarded; otherwise, we will make the mistake of "harming the meaning with words." Naturally, when we express our own theory, we must pay attention to the beauty and power of words and the structure of the text, because if we can express our opinions with the most vivid words and the most perfect writing method, then the effect on theory will inevitably be great. However, this is also a question of how to better express our theory, not a meaning that focuses on scrutinizing words; if you don't do it this way, and you must write "critical articles" for the sake of beautiful words and witty scolding, then no matter how much comfort you get in your personal heart, no matter how you boast about the "wittiness" and "beauty" of your article, in the end, general readers will say that you are "showy but unsubstantial," shallow, and boring!

To be honest, so-called beautiful writing is produced under progressive theory. If you don't grasp progressive theory, then you won't be able to write truly beautiful writing; what you can write is only empty or tasteless absurd writing. If you don't believe it, please write an article centered on supporting the theory of imperialists and see what happens. No matter how good you are at writing, I dare say that the result will inevitably be full of ugliness!

In short, we need theoretical criticism, not abuse, and we don't need "showy but unsubstantial" beautiful writing.

Street Wanderers 275

— By Yefeng

Special Feature

The Shen Bao Circulation Library, Amateur Tutoring School, and Women's Tutoring School Commemorate Mr. Shi Liangcai 276

Mr. Shi Liangcai was assassinated on November 13, 1934, on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway in broad daylight. Besides grief, what else can we say about this case? But Mr. Shi’s death cannot be regarded as an ordinary farewell, saying a few words of mourning like everyone else.

We commemorate and admire Mr. Shi because he was not only the sole leader of the Chinese press but also the sole mentor of Chinese mass education. If Mr. Shi had not prioritized the interests of the masses, Shen Bao would not have its long and glorious history today; if Mr. Shi had not aimed to educate the masses, he would not have established social education undertakings in addition to the newspaper business itself. Therefore, we have to commemorate such a great man, our mentor.

We commemorate and admire Mr. Shi because we know that he came from the masses and understood the sufferings of the people. The Shen Bao Circulation Library, the Amateur Tutoring School, and the Women's Tutoring School were all built on this understanding and became important works of Shen Bao's social education. Therefore, we commemorate this great man, our mentor.

We mourn for Mr. Shi's untimely death, for his sacrifice for social undertakings, which prevented him from dedicating his great aspirations to society to the fullest extent and from serving the disaster-ridden country. We cannot help but mourn the loss of the essence of the country and society!

We commemorate Mr. Shi and mourn him because of his great personality and the most important significance of sacrificing for society. Therefore, we want to commemorate Mr. Shi, not focusing on perfunctory formalities but on another meaning of inheriting his legacy.

Continued on Page 5

Page 23

Stop the lamentation! Stop the wailing! Stop the tears! All are useless! What we need is to actively inherit Mr. Shi's great aspirations, tread the path he has opened, and move forward!

Students who are directly or indirectly related to Shen Bao's social education! The vast readers of the Shen Bao Circulation Library! Do you want to say a final goodbye to Mr. Shi? Are you willing to express your admiration and sorrow before Mr. Shi's image?

Therefore, we students and colleagues who assisted Mr. Shi's education undertakings have initiated this memorial service. The date is set for December 10 (Monday), to be held at the "Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association."

We sincerely hope that all students and the vast readers of the Shen Bao Circulation Library will participate individually at that time.

At the same time, we will also accept literary elegies commemorating Mr. Shi and other souvenirs. We also plan to compile all the writings into a book as a major commemoration. If you have these items, please send them to the Shen Bao Circulation Library at 345 Nanjing Road Continental Department Store or the Shen Bao Women's Tutoring School at 75 Xieqiaonong, Jing'an Temple Road, before December 9.

We do not emphasize form in our commemoration, but at the same time, we cannot do without form! But what we pay special attention to is the meaning of our commemoration, hoping that all those who are prepared to participate in the conference will pay their respects to Mr. Shi with a solemn meaning! To explain their aspirations! To continue Mr. Shi's unfinished business.

We hope that all students who are directly or indirectly related to Shen Bao and the vast readers of the Shen Bao Circulation Library will mobilize to participate in Mr. Shi's memorial service!

Please Pay Attention, Unemployed Friends 277

A Week's Travel Home (3) 278

— Su Gang

It's indeed not an easy task for a large boat of more than 60 feet to turn around in this shallow and narrow Gan River. More than thirty boatmen were tightly gripping their punting poles and pushing. Steam like steamed buns was rising from their heads, the veins on their foreheads bulging like earthworms, and sweat poured down from their heads like water from a mountain stream. The boat owner stood in front of the awning mast, constantly shouting, "Come on! One more punt on this side. Good, swing left!"

He held a four-foot-long smoking pipe in his hand and shouted energetically, sometimes directing the sailors in front and sometimes shouting at the helmsman in the back, his hands and mouth never stopping for a moment. I couldn't help but laugh when I saw his face. I quickly walked over and shouted to him, "Boss!"

He was caught off guard by my sudden shout, and his body swayed. He turned around, saw that it was me, and quickly put on a smile, saying, "You!"

"I think you're working even harder than them! I've been watching you for a long time, and your hands and mouth haven't stopped for a moment!"

"Ah!" He pulled the smoking pipe out of his mouth, sighed, and then said with a smile, "Don't you know the hardship of earning a living? This boat is my family's property, and everyone depends on it for food and drink. If we don't move for a day, we don't eat for a day. If we accidentally hit a hole, it's terrible! They don't care about these things. If the boat breaks down and can't move, they can go to another boat." (To be continued)

Narrative Singing 281

Yao Xiao'an's Pearl Pagoda

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening "Lamenting the Lotus"

The scorching sun brightly illuminates the lotus pond. Tall and graceful, they resemble the Sixth Son. Everyone envies their complete attire of silk. The fluttering dragonflies busily carry fragrance. Deep affection binds the mandarin duck companions. A bitten-arm oath ensures the longevity of their bond, as enduring as the sun and moon. I remember his翩翩 graceful demeanor, like He Lang's appearance. I remember her 綽約 captivating beauty, proud in her waterside village. Leisurely talk praises the enchanting beauty of immortals, with twin blossoms spreading fragrance throughout the world. Alas, temporary joy is difficult to sustain. In an instant, the autumn wind brings a distinct chill. Light silk sleeves are deemed too thin. The opportunistic mandarin ducks no longer behave with decorum. I recall the days when, in emerald sleeves, she rode freely in the wind, once recording her surname to inform Wang Chang. Now, as summer ends and autumn arrives, things are not as desired. Even those withered branches and decaying leaves emit no pleasant fragrance. The fickleness of the world is truly hateful. Looking back, the past is but a dream. I advise the world, do not say that the heat of summer is easily endured. When the autumn chill arrives, you will personally taste the bitter and辛辛 flavors. I lament the lotus flower while also satirizing the world. It is not an intentional insult to the Sixth Son. Like Song Yu, I grieve for autumn out of personal sorrow.

Yu Xiaoxia, Yu Xiaoyun's Jade Dragonfly

New Sound (1380) 6:00 PM to 7:00 PM

Opening "Wu Shi Returns and Kills His Sister-in-law"

Wu Song's nature is fierce and resolute. In a moment, he raises his knife without hesitation. Startled, the neighbors come to dissuade him. Elder Chen explains the details carefully. The hero fears not the laws of the imperial court. With his knife, he kills Jin Lian, ending her life. I say to you respected neighbors, do not be alarmed. Wu Er takes responsibility for his actions alone. He runs through the streets with his knife in an instant, all because Xi Menqing is too wicked. Those who commit adultery with women will not have a good end. He coincidentally encounters Xi Menqing at the tavern. Truly, it is a dragon and tiger fight in the streets. Wu Dalang secretly comes to help. He cleaves Xi Menqing with his knife, ending his life. He goes to the public court to strike the drum. The county magistrate immediately ascends the bench. Mother Wang confesses to her schemes. He scrutinizes the wicked plot and reveals the details. Captain Chao is sentenced to banishment.

Sinology 283

Ms. Wang Bingmei's Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Number Three

Countless mountains and valleys flock to Jingmen, the birthplace of Lady Zhaojun still has a village.

Once gone from the purple terraces to the northern desert, only a green tomb remains facing the twilight.

In paintings, one recognizes her spring breeze face, her jade pendants must return on a moonlit night as a spirit.

For a thousand years, the pipa has played a barbarian tune, clearly conveying resentment in its melodies.

Number Four

The Shu ruler campaigned against Wu, traveling through the Three Gorges, and died in Yong'an Palace in a year of collapse.

Imagining his jade carriage amidst the empty mountains, the jade palace is empty within the wild temple.

Ancient temple cedars and pines are nesting places for water herons, villagers walk by to perform sacrifices every year and season.

The Temple of Marquis Wu is nearby, ruler and minister are worshiped together as one.

Number Five

Zhuge's great name echoes through the universe, the loyal minister's image is solemn and lofty.

His strategic planning divided the land into three, his feather fan has lasted through ten thousand ages of clouds and skies.

Between Bo Zhong, one sees Yi Yin and Lü Shang, his command was decisive, eclipsing Xiao He and Cao Shen.

The fate of the Han Dynasty was ultimately difficult to restore, his resolve was to sacrifice himself to relieve the army's labors.

Parting from Xue Liu and Liu Ba, Two Officials, Again in Jiangzhou Liu Changqing

I never expected to receive a gracious imperial decree, I idly learned drunken songs, knowing nothing of worldly affairs.

The moon is bright over the river, wild geese fly past, the trees fall in Huainan, and there are many Chu mountains.

I am happy to live near the waterside, but I am sad to see my white hair.

Today, we are both old and decrepit, I am ashamed that you still care about the treacherous waves.
